U.S. Fleet Completely Transferred to the Pacific to Monitor the Progress of the Far Eastern Situation, the Navy Does Not Change Its Original Policy 51

(Hampton Roads, USA) The U.S. Combined Fleet concentrated here today to prepare to return to the Pacific. The so-called Atlantic (back door) is now completely open and undefended. The entire fleet is scheduled to set sail tomorrow, with several submarine teams joining along the way. Autumn manoeuvres will be held in the Caribbean Sea. On November 1, the fleet will pass through the Panama Canal. The so-called Combined Fleet is composed of the heavy battleship fleet that has been stationed in the Pacific for many years and the lighter scout fleet that was originally stationed in the Atlantic. Since Japan occupied Manchuria and the Far East, the Combined Fleet has been concentrated in the Pacific for two years. This year, it was transferred to the Atlantic for only six months. At the time, the situation in the Far East was calm, so officials stated that it was to allow naval personnel to take the opportunity to return home. However, observers believed that this was to show Japan that the United States was adopting a defensive posture in the Pacific in order to ease the tense situation in the Far East. The U.S. fleet's return to the Pacific this time is also part of the original plan and should not be seen as a change in policy. However, this move shows that the United States is focusing on its western front, believing that the turmoil in Europe will not immediately affect the U.S.'s position in the Atlantic. Some military experts believe that late autumn and early winter are the most dangerous periods in the Far East. If a Russo-Japanese war breaks out, it will inevitably begin when the northern rivers are frozen solid, so that land troops can move. The United States is therefore transferring its fleet back at this time. There is also a saying that if a war breaks out in Europe, a certain country in the Far East may take the opportunity to attack, so what the U.S. military is worried about is actually the Pacific. The U.S. fleet will also be stationed in the Pacific for a long time in the future, and Britain will have to pay attention to Europe and will have no worries about the East. (16th National Telegram)

Paris Plans to Build a Tall Tower to Improve Air Defences 52

Six Thousand Feet High, Divided into Three Layers

To House Fighter Planes and Three Hundred Cannons

(Paris) Today, the Excelsior pictorial magazine published a plan drawn up by an engineer to build a tall tower of six thousand feet in order to improve France's air defences. This tower is divided into three layers, each of which can house fighter planes, so that they can take off in case of emergency and fight enemy bombers, avoiding the slow ascent of aircraft from the ground at present. The tower can also be equipped with three hundred cannons to fire in all directions. (17th Reuters Dispatch)

Development of Soviet Civil Aviation 53

National Air Routes Extend 50,000 Kilometres

Shortened Transportation and Ethnic Communication

(TASS, Moscow, August 13) August 18 is Aviation Day. Soviet cities and collective farms are actively preparing to celebrate the development of Soviet civil aviation since 1933. In the past five years, the total length of air routes has reached 9,326 kilometres, with over 21,000 passengers and 368 tons of mail and cargo transported. Since 1929, the Soviet Union has been manufacturing its own aircraft and engines, such as the ANT-14, ANT-9, K-5, P-5, and STAL-5. In addition to being used for transportation, aircraft are also widely used in agriculture and forestry, such as pest control, sowing, surveying, and sanitation. The total length of Soviet air routes is now around 50,000 kilometres, with major routes including the Moscow-Vladivostok line, the Moscow-Tbilisi line, and the Moscow-Tashkent line. Soviet air routes have connected all major economic and administrative centres in the country, and have also connected various remote ethnic areas. For example, there are now several air routes in Central Asia. The journey from Stalinabad to Khorog, which previously took 30 days, now takes only four hours. The same is true for the route from Yakutsk to Irkutsk. Previously, this route took 18 days in summer and 30 days in winter, but now it only takes two or three days. During the Second Five-Year Plan, Soviet air routes will increase to 85,000 kilometres, not including local routes. During this period, remote areas such as Central Asia, Kazakhstan, Yakutia, and Siberia will see the greatest development.

(London) Prince George of England's fiancée, Princess Marina of Greece, arrived in England this afternoon from Paris with her parents. She was greeted by 5,000 people in Folkestone. Tens of thousands of people also gathered inside and outside Victoria Station. Authorities dispatched special police forces to maintain order. Prince George returned from Balmoral in the morning and was also on the platform. When the princess arrived, without any formalities, Prince George stepped forward to greet her and they embraced. In the evening, Prince George and Princess Marina went to Balmoral to stay with the King and Queen of England. The platform was once again filled with cheering crowds. As the train departed, the princess leaned out the window to thank the crowd and waved her handkerchief repeatedly. (Reuters Dispatch, 16th)

Late Rice in the Capital Area Also Damaged 71

(Nanjing) According to agricultural experts, the summer in the vicinity of the capital area was severely dry, and many rice plants withered. After autumn, there was continuous wind and rain, which was not a blessing for farmers. At this time, the early rice was waiting to be harvested, and the late rice was in bloom. The heavy rain destroyed the early rice, which was soft and submerged in water. Due to the water immersion, it germinated. The flowers of the late rice were beaten off, resulting in flowering without fruiting. Both early and late rice crops have suffered great damage this year. (Special Dispatch, 17th)

Legal Interpretation of Marriage 72

(Nanjing) The Belgian envoy Ji Youmu requested the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to interpret whether marriages performed in China according to religious rites, such as Catholicism, Christianity, and Judaism, are recognized as valid under Chinese law. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs forwarded the request to the Ministry of Judicial Administration for consultation. After seeking opinions, a response was sent to the Belgian envoy, stating in essence that if a marriage ceremony is held in a church, the ceremony is public, and there is a priest or pastor officiating, and if there are other witnesses, the total number being two or more, it meets the conditions stipulated in Article 982 of the Family Law of the Civil Code of China (the marriage ceremony has a public ceremony and two or more witnesses), it can be considered valid. (Special Dispatch, 17th)

Qian Wang Cables Report on the Resolution of the Liao Division 109

Guangzhou Correspondence: Recently, the He Long bandit gang has been harassing Guizhou and has not yet been suppressed, while the Xiao Ke communist bandits have crossed western Hunan and invaded the border of Guangxi, plotting to join forces with the He Long department of Guizhou bandits. Just as the Guizhou border defense situation was extremely tense, news suddenly came that internal disputes had arisen again in Guizhou Province. The Guizhou army Wang (Jialie) and You (Guocai) combined and then separated. At the end of last month, You Guocai's Liao Huai-zhong division was completely resolved by Wang Jialie's troops. Yesterday, a telegram was received from Wang Jialie, reporting the inside story as follows: ( (Salutations omitted) Both are informed, confidential: After investigating the third division commander, Liao Huaizhong, he indiscriminately recruited bandits and refused to be incorporated. Furthermore, he fabricated words to discredit, and acted freely. As the Red Bandits were growing day by day, he could only accommodate the facts and treat them with indulgence. He was ordered to return to station in Yanhe Yinjiang to jointly suppress the bandits. Unexpectedly, the various bandit suppression troops defeated the bandit He Long, who retreated to the Ganchuanxiang junction in the area of Ganlongkou Xieyaojie. Just as he was preparing to unite with friendly troops from neighboring provinces to encircle and annihilate them, the division commander dared to collude with the Red Bandits and disrupt the rear defense, causing He Long to take the opportunity to break through and counterattack Si (Nan) Yin (Jiang), resulting in the failure of the bandit suppression plan. Moreover, the Red Bandit Xiao Ke rushed into Hunan and fled in a hurry. He was deeply afraid that it would harm the border area, so he would give the bandits a chance to spread. He immediately ordered the various bandit suppression troops to thoroughly resolve the department in order to avoid hindering the work of suppressing the Reds. Fortunately, the resolution was complete. Liao (Huaizhong) only left alone. The various armies continued to advance towards the bandit area, with daily progress. In addition to informing the friendly troops of neighboring provinces and issuing orders to all departments of our army, I hereby send a telegram to report. Wang Jialie, Qing (September), printed. Overview of Sino-Malaysian Trade in the First Half of the Year 110

Exports Exceed Imports by Over 1.28 Million Yuan

(Singapore Correspondence) Trade statistics for the first half of this year, from January to June inclusive, between the British Malaya in the Nanyang Islands and various ports in China have already been published. A general report is hereby specially made for the reference of domestic industrial and commercial circles. However, to reduce the number of digits, figures below a thousand are generally omitted.

It is found that the total value of goods imported into China from the Federated Malay States and the Straits Settlements in the first half of this year was 6,229,000 yuan in national currency, accounting for 1.09 per cent of China's total imports. The total value of Chinese goods transported to the Federated Malay States and the Straits Settlements was 7,518,000 yuan in national currency, accounting for 2.80 per cent of China's total exports, resulting in a surplus of 1,289,000 yuan. The number of Chinese residing in British Malaya totals more than 1.7 million, and their daily necessities are mostly Chinese goods. Therefore, for decades, China's trade with Malaya has consistently shown a surplus. However, since the September 18th Incident, when the four northeastern provinces were forcibly occupied by the Japanese, China's exports to Malaya have been greatly affected, resulting in a shift from surplus to deficit in Sino-Malaysian trade in 1932 and 1933, which was very unfavorable to China. It was not until the first half of this year that the surplus status was restored, which can be considered a considerable improvement. However, given the large Chinese population overseas, this minimal surplus cannot satisfy us.

In the first half of this year, the main goods transported from Malaya to China and their values were: tin ingots and blocks, approximately 122,000 Haikwan taels (hereinafter the same); sea cucumbers, 164,000; dried shrimp and shrimp paste, 30,000; fish and seafood products, 101,000; preserved meat and daily necessities, 83,000; rice, 39,000; miscellaneous grains and flour, 35,000; fruits, 25,000; medicinal materials and spices, 245,000; pharmaceuticals, 39,000; dyes and colors, 92,000; coconut oil, 313,000; rubber and wax, 29,000; sole leather, 33,000; heavy timber, 263,000; railway sleepers, 6,000; teak, 117,000; sandalwood, 52,000; timber, 26,000; rattan, 376,000; rubber boots and shoes, 18,000; rubber tires, 4,000; rubber and rubber products, 734,000; other items, 91,000. The value of the above imported goods into China is calculated in Haikwan taels. In the first half of this year, according to the average price in Shanghai, each Haikwan tael was equivalent to 1.971 yuan in national currency.

As for the total value of Chinese goods transported to Malaya in the first half of this year, it is also worth noting. According to statistics, fresh eggs amounted to approximately 69,000 yuan (hereinafter the same); eggs and egg products, 42,000; processed meat, 56,000; fish and seafood products, 39,000; lard, 75,000; soybeans, 2,000; beans and peas, 144,000; miscellaneous grains and flour, 21,000; bean cakes, 77,000; seed cakes and miscellaneous grain products, 24,000; fruits, 490,000; medicinal materials and spices, 102,000; peanut oil, 144,000; green tea, 99,000; cigarettes, 55,000; tobacco, 59,000; vermicelli and macaroni, 94,000; vegetables and plant products, 101,000; coal, 13,000; paper, 643,000; silk fabrics and embroidered items, 48,000; silk embroidery, 96,000; lace ornaments, 21,000; coarse twill fabrics, 43,000; market cloth and coarse cloth, 52,000; native cloth, 570,000; pure silk satins, 295,000; pure artificial silk satins, 176,000; silk fabric, 16,000; textiles and clothing parts, 742,000; metals and metal products, 74,000; porcelain, 29,000; clay, sand, stone, and their products, 38,000; chemicals and chemical products, 416,000; sugarcane and cane sugar, 75,000; other items, totaling approximately 336,000 yuan.

The Righteous Army Led by Zhao Shangzhi Launches a Surprise Attack on a Puppet Ship 112

The Righteous Army's Elite Forces Wreak Havoc, Achieving Significant Results in Attacking Ships

Several Japanese Soldiers Killed in a Bloody Battle on the Songhua River

The City of Harbin Plunged into Terror as the Puppet Ship Returns

(Changchun Correspondence) In order to preserve Baoli, the righteous armies on all fronts in eastern Jilin have changed their strategies, with all cadres lying in wait in the nearby mountains and dense forests, awaiting an opportunity for a major offensive. However, in order to maintain the status quo and prevent shortages of military supplies, elite troops from each unit, fully equipped with weapons and ammunition, have been selected to form dozens of Righteous Army Advance Regiments. Each regiment is organized with a maximum of about 100 men, and they go to the railway and along the river, disguised as workers and travelers, launching surprise attacks that are unpredictable, creating multiple incidents of overturning trains and attacking ships, capturing and killing many Japanese soldiers. This is even more effective than the disorganized large armies of the righteous army. Although there are many armored trains and gunboats of the Japanese and puppet railway and maritime guards, the Righteous Army is elusive and their strategies are unpredictable. Therefore, the Japanese and puppet troops are exhausted, and the state of terror along the railway and on ships, and the occurrence of incidents, have not diminished. Recently, the Righteous Army launched another heroic act of surprise attack on a puppet ship near Di Da Zui Zi, seven kilometers downstream of the Songhua River from Harbin. On the 9th of this month, more than 30 members of the Righteous Army Advance Regiment led by Zhao Shangzhi, disguised as passengers and hiding weapons, boarded the puppet ship Yingkou Maru in Harbin. When they arrived at Di Da Zui Zi, they pulled out pistols to intimidate other passengers and crew members, instructing them to temporarily stop the ship, and immediately began searching for Japanese. Nearby, many sailing boats were ambushed in advance, full of Righteous Army soldiers, using a war strategy of attacking from inside and outside, causing the ship to fall into great chaos. Fighting sounds were heard in all the cabins. As a result, Sakaguchi, the puppet police chief of Hulin, killed three members of the Righteous Army, but because he ran out of bullets, he was eventually killed by the Righteous Army. Iwanaga Shizuo, the puppet councillor of Hulin County, jumped into the river and drowned. In addition, two brave men from the Gaohe County Public Office were seriously injured. In addition, two Japanese were missing, and Japanese women were captured. Two crew members and one soldier were also killed. More than 30 people were captured by the Righteous Army for ransom, and all the goods were taken away for military use. The Righteous Army left in sailing boats at 1:00 am the next morning. The surviving crew members only opened the ship to Harbin at 10:00 am. Blood flowed like rivers in the ship, and corpses lay everywhere, making the situation very tragic. Rumors spread in Harbin for a time, plunging the city into a state of terror. It was generally said that the Japanese gunboats patrolling the river could not eliminate the disaster in advance, which was extremely useless. The public opinion of the whole city also recognized that the power of the Righteous Army was inviolable, so people's hearts were extremely excited. (Northeast News Agency)

Banditry Rampant Again in Luanyu Area 113

Robberies Occur in Qinhuangdao in Broad Daylight

Japanese and Korean Rogues Protect Criminals

(Tianjin Correspondence) Banditry in various places in eastern Tianjin has become increasingly rampant since the beginning of the Green Gauze Uprising. It is no longer surprising that bandits rob in towns during the day. Outside the towns, bandits are stationed, either in large or small groups, and there are more that cannot be counted. The number of bandits in large groups is two or three hundred, and in small groups, sixty or seventy. Kidnapping and extortion have made people unable to make a living. The security teams stationed by us in the Luanyu and Jiji-Mi areas of eastern Tianjin have a limited number of people, and only about half of them are truly dedicated to serving and vigorously suppressing bandits. The remaining half, not causing trouble to the local area and supplying bandits, is already considered to be the top of military discipline. If they are held accountable for serving the local area and defending merchants and people, it is difficult to say anything. The reason for the proliferation of bandits is first, because this year, the counties in northern Hebei suffered drought followed by floods, and the autumn harvest was poor, and the countryside was desolate; second, because Japanese and Korean rogues gathered and set up opium and gambling institutions everywhere, farmers were lured into them, their families were ruined, and those who abandoned agriculture became increasingly numerous. Therefore, there are fewer producers, and as a result of profit-sharing, a wind of seizing by force and plundering by force has evolved. Moreover, because the non-armed zone has special circumstances, offenders often seek foreign aid and have nothing to fear. Therefore, banditry has become increasingly rampant. The people of Zhoucun Village, Ji County, even form groups to paint their faces and rob silently at night. Although they know each other clearly, they do not report to the authorities. The number of bandits is the highest in any county. Banditry is even more rampant in Qinhuangdao City. Street robberies occur on quiet streets in broad daylight. The victims immediately report to the police, but they dare not chase after the robbers as they flee. Japanese and Korean rogues in the area have dozens of foreign firms, which not only sell morphine, heroin, and other highly toxic drugs, but also sell guns and ammunition. If bandits who cannot afford to buy guns are introduced by two or three accomplices, they can rent a gun for use. After the crime, the proceeds are split four to six. If the government's search and arrest are too urgent, they can temporarily hide in their foreign firms, which are responsible for their protection. As a result, the public security is chaotic, and it is almost impossible for the Public Security Bureau to maintain it. Outside Yu Pass, there are more than 20 large and small groups of bandits, each with 30 to 200 men. The area within three miles outside the city is the bandit-controlled area. Most of the police are unarmed. Last month, after negotiations by Su Yuqi, Director of the Public Security Bureau, the Japanese side agreed to increase 50 large guns. However, there are only 50 large guns and 20 pistols for more than 200 police officers in Yuguan, which is not enough to maintain the city, let alone take care of the outside of the city. Therefore, gunshots are constantly heard outside the city walls every night. At about 6:00 pm, there are few pedestrians outside the south and west gates. The Japanese special service agencies and the police stations of the Japanese Kwantung Army only pay attention to preventing incidents in the city and do not care about the fact that our people outside the city cannot sleep peacefully. Therefore, the area east of Tangshan is purely a world of bandits. (13th)

The Amoy Taiwanese Murder Case Resolved 114

Detectives and Taiwanese Reach Settlement Terms

(Xiamen Correspondence) On the evening of August 31, a conflict occurred among tourists at the Mei Zhou Tea House on Fuyu Road, He-He Road, and Taiwanese Lin Guimu (Jiadong) was shot and killed. At that time, Fang Jinpan, Deputy Captain of the Second Detective Team of the Criminal Investigation Division of the Public Security Bureau, led detectives to the scene to suppress the situation. Afterwards, the Taiwanese side pointed out that Lin Guimu was killed by a certain detective. Therefore, on the night of the 2nd, thugs shot and wounded Detective Lin Bo of the First Team at the Yuyan Coffee Shop on Siming South Road. Lin was seriously injured by three bullets. The thugs who fired the shots were identified as Taiwanese, and Lin Bo himself identified them as Taiwanese he knew well. After these two cases occurred one after another, people in the market were panicked, fearing that there would be further conflicts between the two sides. The Japanese consul made representations to the Public Security Bureau regarding the death of Lin Guimu, and the Public Security Bureau also made representations to the Japanese consul. However, after the night of the 2nd, Wang Guqing, Director of the Public Security Bureau, and Ogawa Yonosuke, Chief of the Japanese Police Station, consulted with each other and agreed that both sides should restrain themselves and not make any changes before the case was resolved, so no further conflicts occurred. A private individual came forward to mediate between the detectives and the Taiwanese. However, the conditions put forward by both sides were extremely tough, and the perpetrators of both cases had fled the scene, leaving no evidence. Therefore, neither side would give in, and it remained unresolved for more than ten days. After repeated mediation by "public relatives" (Xiamen calls mediators "public relatives"), the terms were finally agreed upon on the evening of the 11th. On the evening of the 13th, another meeting was held, and from 9:00 pm to 1:00 am the next morning (14th), the representatives of both sides and the "public relatives" signed three reconciliation agreements, and each party held two copies. The original text of the reconciliation agreement is transcribed as follows: In the case of the shooting and killing of Taiwanese Lin Jiadong, the case was invited by the variable side on the afternoon of September 11th this year, together with "public relatives" Wu Yachun, Liu Zemin, Xie Shaozeng, and Gu Zhen, etc., and Taiwanese representatives He Xinghua, Lin Qingcheng, Wu Tianci, Wang Haisheng, Lin Zhigao, Zheng Deming, and Zhang Weiyuan, and detective representatives Lin Danian and Chen Qiucheng, etc., to Zhang Guanshu to discuss five conditions, which were agreed upon by both parties, and this agreement was established on this (13th) day, and its origin is recorded as above. Xiamen Lin Case Reconciliation Meeting, time: 9:00 pm, September 13, 23rd year of the Republic of China; location: Sanyou Restaurant, Siming South Road; Taiwanese representatives present: He Xinghua, Wu Tianci, Lin Zhigao, Zhang Weiyuan, Wang Haisheng, Chen Chunmu, Lin Qingcheng, Zhang Guanshu, Chen Changfu, Zheng Deming; detective representatives present: Lin Danian; "public relatives" Wu Yachun, Hu Zhen, Liu Zemin, Xie Shaozeng, Hong Xiaochun, Chen Ruiqing, Chen Qiucheng, Yan Yan, Lu Tianbao, and Huang Yishou; the reconciliation conditions are as follows: (1) The case of the shooting and killing of Taiwanese Lin Jiadong (the authorities now know who the perpetrator is) shall be handled by the Public Security Bureau immediately detaining the principal offender and accomplices and severely punishing them according to law. (2) "Public relatives" shall be engaged to raise 1,000 yuan for Lin Jiadong's funeral expenses. (3) The case of the shooting and wounding of Detective Lin Bo shall be handled according to law after the authorities have investigated the truth. (4) After this case is resolved, personnel from both sides shall not engage in similar incidents again to show friendship. (5) Regarding the shooting and killing of Lin Jiadong, it was caused by Fang Jinpan's inability to maintain order when he led the team to suppress the situation, resulting in the death. He voluntarily publishes an apology to the Taiwanese community to clarify his intentions. In addition to the above five articles, the matter will be handled by the official authorities of both sides. Taiwanese representatives He Xinghua, Wu Tianci, Lin Zhigao, Zhang Weiyuan, Wang Haisheng, Chen Chunmu, Lin Qingcheng, Zhang Guanshu, Chen Changfu, Zheng Deming; detective representative Lin Danian; "public relatives" Wu Yachun, Hu Zhen, Xie Shaozeng, Liu Zemin, Hong Xiaochun, Chen Ruiqing, Chen Qiucheng, Yan Dayuan, Lu Tianbao, and Huang Yishou, September 13, 23rd year of the Republic of China. Attached is the draft of Fang Jinpan's (Apology Statement) in its original text as follows: (In the case of the shooting and killing of Taiwanese Lin Jiadong, Jinpan led the team to suppress the situation, but was unable to maintain order at the time, resulting in the death. I feel deeply uneasy and hereby publish an apology to the Taiwanese community to clarify my intentions. Fang Jinpan, September 13, 23rd year of the Republic of China). At this point, the case between the Taiwanese and the detectives has been resolved. The Public Security Bureau and the Japanese consul only performed routine official duties and handled the matter in accordance with this agreement, which was also concluded. However, Lin Bo has already expressed dissatisfaction with the fact that the reconciliation agreement only stated that his shooting injury would be investigated and handled, leaving the matter unresolved.

Overview of the Drought in Anhui Province 115

Approximately 20 Million Mu or More of Disaster-Stricken Fields

More Than 10 Million Disaster Victims

(Anqing Correspondence) The drought in Anhui Province this year has affected almost the entire province. Currently, 46 counties, including Huaining, have reported disasters. The disaster-stricken fields and population account for more than one-half of the total in the province. Central and southern Anhui have always been the main rice-producing areas, and the rice varieties are mostly early-maturing and mid-maturing. This year, from growth to fruiting, they have been in a drought period, and the damage is extremely severe. Northern Anhui mostly grows miscellaneous grains, such as broad beans and sesame, either due to lack of rain or withered after planting, and the disaster is also severe. In mid-June and July, farmers sold their clothes and used all their savings to hire workers to draw water from ponds and canals to maintain a lifeline for farming, hoping to reap the autumn harvest in one out of ten thousand. By August, not only did the farmers have nothing left, but they were also exhausted from poverty and illness and unable to draw water, and the water sources were also mostly exhausted, making it impossible to draw water for rescue, and they were almost completely trapped in despair. In order to provide disaster relief, the provincial government has organized a People's Food Regulation Committee and sent personnel to various counties to investigate the disaster situation. According to the investigation and statistics of 20 counties, including Wuhu, the disaster-stricken farmland has reached 10,333,000 mu or more, and the estimated number of disaster victims has reached 4,154,000 or more. Based on this estimate, the number of disaster-stricken fields in the 46 counties affected by the drought in the province should be between 20 million and 25 million mu, and the number of disaster victims should be more than 10 million. It is further estimated that the loss of agricultural products, using a minimum of 20 million mu as the standard, of which three-fifths are paddy fields, which are completely planted with rice, and each mu normally yields four stones of rice, and this year, approximately 48 million stones of rice have been lost. In addition, two-fifths of the dry land, approximately 5 million stones of millet, 3 million stones of beans, and more than 10 million stones of sesame seeds have been lost. To sum up, these are the overview and estimates of the drought in Anhui Province. The detailed situation still needs to be based on the statistics after the completion of the investigation by all the disaster investigation committee members. The statistics of the disaster-stricken fields and the population of disaster victims in the 20 counties, including Wuhu, which have already been reported, are listed below:

(September 15)

Wang Zhan Yuan Passed Away 116

享年七十四歲 (Enjoyed a life of 74 years)

胃疾不治而死 (Died of an Untreatable Stomach Ailment)

天津通信 (Tianjin Correspondence) Former Inspector General of Hunan and Hubei Provinces, Military Governor and concurrently Governor of Hubei Province, Wang Zhan Yuan, died of an untreatable stomach ailment at 4 a.m. this morning at his residence on 14th Road in the British Concession of Tianjin. After his family issued mourning notices, former colleagues and subordinates, such as Sun Chuanfang, Jin Yunpeng, Yun E, Qi Xieyuan, and Pan Fu, all rushed to offer condolences and help with the funeral arrangements. Wang suffered from stomach ailments for many years, with periods of remission and relapse, but the condition worsened this spring. Wang did not take it seriously until two months ago, when he fell ill and could not get out of bed. He then sought treatment from famous Chinese and Western doctors in Beijing and Tianjin, but it was too late. His family and friends have scheduled the funeral for the 15th of this month, with a seven-day mourning period before transporting the coffin back to his ancestral home in Shandong Province. Wang, whose courtesy name was Zichun, originally named Xian, was a native of Guanxian County, Shandong Province. He was born on the 11th day of the first month of the tenth year of the Xianfeng era of the Qing Dynasty and died at the age of 74. In the fifth year of the Guangxu era, he joined the right battalion of the Ming army as a soldier. In August of the twelfth year, he was selected to study at the Beiyang Military Academy. After graduating in the eighteenth year of Guangxu, he returned to military service and rose through the ranks to become the commanding officer of the First Standard of the First Army. During the Sino-Japanese War, Wang was under the command of Liu Mingchuan of the Xiang Army and fought in the Dalian and Yingkou areas, earning considerable merit. In the late Qing Dynasty, he rose to the rank of commander of the Second Army. In the early Republic of China, he was reorganized as the Second Division and served as its commander with the rank of lieutenant general. In July of the second year of the Republic, he was awarded the title of general. In the spring of the sixth year, he was appointed commander-in-chief for the suppression of bandits in Henan and Anhui, leading troops to quell the White Wolf bandit rebellion. In May of the same year, he was promoted to assistant to the military affairs of Hubei. In September of the ninth year of the Republic, he was promoted to military governor of Hubei and awarded the title of Zhuangwei General. In January of the fifth year, he was awarded the title of Xiangwu General. In July, he was appointed military governor and concurrently governor of Hubei and, in the ninth year, Inspector General of Hunan and Hubei. In the tenth year of the Republic, he retired to Tianjin, where he invested heavily in the Tianjin market, factories, mines, and various entertainment venues. Wang lived a simple life and owned real estate through his various businesses in Tianjin. Although he employed people to manage his affairs, he did not fully trust them and personally inspected them every morning. The people of Tianjin knew him as "Lord Wang the Seventh," no longer referring to his official title or name, but treating him as an elder. Even while ill, Wang continued to make inspections, ignoring his family's advice. In the early spring, his condition worsened, and he had difficulty walking, but he was still reluctant to spend money on medical treatment. It was not until his condition became critical that his family disobeyed his wishes and invited famous doctors from Beijing to diagnose him, spending more than 300,000 in two months. His nephews and nieces did not dare to tell Wang the truth, only reporting expenses of two or three thousand, but Wang still frowned upon hearing this. Wang's wife passed away early. He had three sons, Zhang Zekuan, Shu Zeshu, and He Zehe, all of whom are doing well. His nephew Zepei once served as the director of the Xinhe Commercial Bureau. His estate is estimated to be worth around three million, mostly in Tianjin land and stocks. In summary, Wang's life was neither exceptionally good nor bad. However, before the founding of the Republic, he followed Duan Zhigui in retreating to Baoding, contacted the revolutionary army of Li Yuanhong, and promoted the republic. During the Pingyuan Church Case in the sixth year of the Republic, he advocated for lenient handling, saving countless lives. His endorsement of troop reduction in the tenth year of the Republic were all notable achievements. (14th)

Impersonating a Drug Enforcement Officer Arrested 117

（松江） (Songjiang) In the coastal towns of Punan County, the use of red pills is rampant, and the number of people addicted is increasing daily. Unscrupulous individuals are taking advantage of this situation to manufacture and sell them privately. Recently, a villager named Zhang bought red pills from a man named Weng. On his way out, he was stopped by someone impersonating a drug enforcement officer, who took him back to Weng's house and extorted over four hundred yuan, which they divided among themselves. The Public Security Bureau learned of this incident and secretly sent police officers to Caojing to investigate. They arrested Shen Xingsheng, Shen Bojun, Gu Huanzhang, Wu Zhonghua, and four others, who were taken back to the county bureau for interrogation and held under strict guard. It is unknown how this matter will be resolved.

Pharmacist's Dissection of Newborn Nephew Causes Tragedy 118

(嘉定) (Jiading) The wife of Zhang Zhaoxi, the secretary of the Jiading County Government, gave birth at around 10:00 AM on the 9th of this month. They invited Tong Mingya, a midwife from the Jiading People's Hospital, to assist with the delivery. Ms. Tong brought her assistant, Ms. Yang Suyue, along with the necessary equipment. Upon arriving, they noticed a young man in the delivery room. Both Ms. Tong and Ms. Yang were surprised and inquired about his identity. They learned that his name was Wu Dangchun and that he was the doctor hired by the family. He was also a pharmacist at the Jiading Drug Rehabilitation Center and the brother-in-law of Secretary Zhang's wife. His sister was the one giving birth. At that time, the wife of Magistrate Xu was also in the room, as she was the sister of the one giving birth. Thus, Wu was also the brother-in-law of Magistrate Xu. Ms. Tong and the others considered themselves to be mere midwives, while Wu Dangchun was a formal doctor, a civil servant, and a close relative of the one giving birth. They naturally treated him with respect. Before the birth, the patient asked for a "labor-inducing injection," which was administered by Dr. Wu. When the baby was born, it didn't cry at first, which is common during childbirth. Ms. Yang held the baby upside down and gently patted its bottom, which caused it to make a faint sound. However, Dr. Wu suddenly claimed that this method would not save the baby and that Ms. Tong and Ms. Yang should focus on caring for the mother while he took care of the baby. Ms. Tong and Ms. Yang believed that as a doctor, Wu's experience and knowledge were superior to theirs. The mother also sided with her brother and disapproved of Ms. Yang's method of holding the baby upside down and gently patting it. Therefore, they handed the baby over to Wu. Ms. Tong and Ms. Yang focused on caring for the mother. After everything was finished, they saw the baby placed on a side bed, wrapped in a towel, without making a sound. They were shocked and asked Wu about it. Wu said that he had given the baby a stimulant injection, but it was too late to save it. Ms. Tong and Ms. Yang were disappointed when leaving. Wu then told Ms. Tong and Ms. Yang to take the baby with them. When they refused, Wu said, "We doctors should always be researching. Since this child died of breath-holding, we should examine it in detail to find out why. Please take it to your hospital, and I will come soon to examine it closely to find out the cause. This is something that medical students should do." Ms. Tong and Ms. Yang had no choice but to take the dead baby to the hospital. Soon after, Wu arrived at the hospital and sat in the reception room, inspecting the dead baby. It happened to be a Sunday, and because of financial constraints, the hospital did not have a resident doctor. Every Sunday, a doctor from the same hometown would take turns returning to Jiading from Shanghai to provide medical services at the hospital. As a result, many people were seeking medical attention, and the assistants were busy helping with prescriptions. They were unaware that the dead baby in the reception room was being subjected to a slow and painful dismemberment. Ms. Jin Ruizhen, a midwife at the hospital, happened to go to the reception room and saw a bloody mess. The so-called Dr. Wu Leichun was holding a sharp blade and dissecting the baby's feet. Ms. Jin was puzzled and asked Wu, "Is this a dissection?" Jin knew that although she had not practiced dissection, she had studied anatomy books and had never seen anyone dissect from the lower body first. She found it strange, but because he was a doctor and a civil servant, she dared not criticize him. Then, he cut open the abdomen and took out the heart and liver, and the heart was still beating. She asked Wu, "This baby doesn't seem to be dead yet. Why are you dissecting it without permission?" Wu replied, "What do you know? The proverb says, 'Even when a person is dead, the heart doesn't die.' The heart often continues to beat even three days after death." Although Jin agreed, she suspected him. She went out and told her colleagues. Xu Jihua, a female doctor on duty at the hospital, heard this and was shocked. She went to the reception room to see what had happened and found that none of his methods were correct. She questioned Wu about which medical school he had graduated from. Wu's face turned red, and he stammered, "I... I studied it at home." Xu rebuked him. Wu then collected the baby's bones and flesh and left. This incident happened a week ago, but the people in the hospital kept it a secret because Wu was related to the magistrate. However, the news eventually leaked out, causing a great uproar in society. Everyone believed that since Wu was a doctor, his obstruction of the emergency measures of holding the baby upside down and gently patting it when the baby didn't cry after birth was already strange. His unauthorized dissection under the guise of examination was even more bizarre, and the fact that the dissection was not performed properly was even more astonishing. It was also heard that Wu had told someone that a set of baby bones was worth 400 yuan, and he had taken it with him, as if he was trying to profit from it. The dead baby was Wu's nephew. If that is the case, his intentions are even more questionable. This is truly an outrageous incident.

(Suzhou) Four People Detained for the Dahua Paper Mill Case and Taken to the Public Security Bureau 119

Regarding the Dahua Paper Mill incident, the county government instructed the Chamber of Commerce to encourage resumption of work and at the same time, implement the opening of another river channel to provide for the city's water supply. Meanwhile, the Public Security Bureau was ordered to arrest the instigators. Currently, the town's Public Security Sub-bureau, on the 16th, arrested Ye Dabao, the owner of a mat shop at the entrance of Zhu Jia Nong; Zhang Guisheng from Hexinglong Mat Shop; Zhang Chuan'gen, a shop assistant from Li Nanshan Mat Shop; and Tang Weichen's brother, Tang Genshan. Zhang and Li were immediately sent to the city's Public Security Bureau, while Tang and Ye were released on bail, with an order to hand over Tang Weichen and Ye's two sons, Shuigen and Gensheng.

Zhou Shugu Tower Robbery Case Solved 120

The robbery that occurred at Zhou Shugu's tower in Hulong Street, with the loss of over ten thousand yuan in cash and banknotes, has been solved within five days by the Water and Land Public Security authorities. Shao, a detective from the 2nd District Water Police, and others, captured two men wearing blue short jackets near Yadan Bridge outside Changmen. They were immediately detained for questioning. One of them, Chen Axian, claimed that he had embezzled dozens of bolts of cloth from a cloth factory in Shanghai and sold them for cash to spend in Suzhou, denying the robbery. The other, Lu Chenglong, also denied the robbery. The police then escorted the two suspects to the Zhou family to be identified. Zhou Bingkun, the victim, identified Chen Mingxian as the robber, but Lu Chenglong was not present at the scene. After repeated questioning, Chen Axian confessed and revealed the names of several accomplices hiding in Shanghai. Captain Li has already sent detectives to Shanghai to arrest them.

Plan to Build the Suzhou-Jiaxing Railway 121

The Ministry of Railways is actively surveying the route for the Suzhou-Jiaxing Railway. The route roughly follows the Suzhou-Jiaxing highway, but in Zhejiang Province, it bypasses Shuangqiao, and in Suzhou, it bypasses Baodai Bridge. Instead, it goes directly to Fengmen and Loumen via Baodai Bridge and connects with the Beijing-Shanghai Railway at Guandu Li. The entire line is about eighty kilometers long. In addition to the Fengmen station in Jiaxing and Suzhou, there are six intermediate stations planned: Wanggangjing, Shengze, Pingwang, Beitan, Wujiang, and Yishan. Three large iron bridges will be built at Pingwang, Liling, and east of Baodai Bridge. The total cost of the bridges and roads is estimated to be over four million yuan, and the entire line is expected to be completed and open to traffic within two years.

Hengtang Township Robbery Case 122

At around 4:00 AM yesterday (the 17th), more than ten bandits armed with guns suddenly arrived at the Zhuangbin area of the Twelfth District of Hengtang Township, Suzhou. They robbed the homes of Hu Renjin at number 14 and Mi Pangen at number 15, injuring the victims and taking away about three hundred yuan in loot.

Wuxi-Chengdu and Wuxi-Suzhou Roads Renamed Chengdu-Suzhou Road 123

(Wuxi) The National Economic Commission's Highway Department, in order to regulate highways in the five provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Fujian, and Jiangxi, has specially numbered and renamed all completed, under construction, and planned national and branch lines in the five provinces. The first line is the Beijing-Shanghai National Highway, including the Nanjing-Yixing and Yixing-Wuxi-Shanghai roads. The second line is the Beijing-Fujian National Highway, including the Yixing-Hangzhou and Hangzhou-Fujian roads, passing through Cao'e River and Tiantai into Fujian. The Wuxi-Chengdu and Suzhou-Wuxi sections are the 152nd branch line, and their name will be changed to Chengdu-Suzhou Road. The Wuxi-Chengdu Long-Distance Bus Company received the official order yesterday, along with a detailed map of the five provinces' highways, instructing them to comply.

Dredging the North Lane River Channel 124

The river near the Diaogiao and Huangniqiao areas outside the North Gate of the county has been silted up for years, making it impassable. The recent drought has made it impossible for boats to travel, disrupting transportation and causing water shortages. The Daqiao Township Office and merchants such as Chen Zhongying and Zhou Weichen, recognizing the severity of the situation, have raised funds and hired workers to dredge the river. The Huangniqiao section has already been completed, and the Diaogiao River section was dammed yesterday to begin pumping water. Work will begin today (the 18th). The total cost of the project is estimated to be over five hundred yuan. At the same time, the Beita Rice Industry is also planning to dredge the river near Xiaosan Liqiao to facilitate transportation.

Land Survey Team Concludes Operations 125

The land survey in the county, led by Zhou Houxi, the leader of the Wuxi branch of the Provincial Land Survey Team, has been underway for over a year. The land survey in the third district has been completed. Due to changes in the provincial land survey plan, aerial surveying will be implemented, which is faster and more efficient. The Provincial Land Bureau has ordered the team to conclude its operations and transfer the team to Danyang County. After receiving the order, Zhou, the team leader, instructed the surveyors and drafters to expedite the conclusion of operations, which must be completed by the end of the month.

Jiangnan Counties Hit by Another Rain Disaster 126

(Zhenjiang) Jiangnan counties suffered from a severe summer drought, with cracked fields and withered crops, resulting in an unprecedented disaster. Fortunately, officials and civilians worked together to draw water from rivers and lakes to irrigate the fields and replant drought-resistant crops in the hopes of salvaging what they could. Since autumn, the weather has been relatively favorable, with timely rainfall, and the land has become moist again. Farmers were happy, believing they could still salvage something. However, recently, there have been heavy downpours, often lasting all day. The rain was particularly heavy in the last two days, as if the Milky Way was pouring down, like a waterfall hanging in the air. The total rainfall in the past few days has been over a foot. Low-lying fields have become a vast expanse of water. Drought-resistant crops such as cotton, beans, buckwheat, wheat, and sweet potatoes cannot withstand excessive rain, which will severely damage the harvest. Even this meager harvest is unattainable, and the common people will truly have nothing to live on. Although the harvest in Jiangbei counties this year is still abundant, the heavy rain has caused the Yi and Huai rivers to rise rapidly, posing an imminent threat to the levees along the Yellow River, which is threatening to invade the old canal.

Suzhou Highway Authority Borrows Money to Purchase Vehicles 127

The Suzhou Construction Department's Highway Administration is planning to add twenty to thirty passenger car chassis and two sedans to its fleet, as its current vehicles are insufficient to meet the needs of its expanding operations. This is being done to develop transportation and boost public operations. They have borrowed 120,000 yuan from Jiangsu and Farmers' Bank. It's reported that while the Highway Adminstration hasn't signed the contract, it is largely agreed upon. Yesterday they sent a letter to over ten automibile firms including Shanghai DaLi, He Jinlong, Feiyou, Huali, Huitanla, Meitong, Madi, Haifeng, Feixing, China, Hezhong, and Nanjing DaXia, Wanfang and many others to inquire about available models. They requested car model, manufacture year, chassis wheelbase length, gross vehicle weight, number of cylinders, horsepower, brand of tire, tire size, and lowest price, and they request detailed written reply within five days with car illustrations and detailed specification.

Drought-Stricken Farmland in Yiqu District 128

(Jiangyin) Due to the severe drought this summer, the provincial government ordered the county to investigate the affected farmland. In the Yiqu District, out of the original 76 townships with 138,767 mu of farmland, Li Dechen, the district chief of Yiqu, reported to the county that 42 townships, covering an area of 28 square li, with 15,297.92 mu of farmland, were affected by the drought, impacting 24,458 people and resulting in a loss of 40,310 dan of rice and 1,964 shi of other grains.

Bandits Set Fire and Loot Liujiagou 129

(Gaoyou) Several days ago, in the Liujiagou area near Linze in the Fifth District of this county, which is within the territory of Xinghua, bandits kidnapped sixteen people in Xinghua. They were intercepted by the local self-defense corps, and the bandits fled in disarray, harboring resentment. At around 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon, a band of over two hundred bandits suddenly arrived, traveling on multiple boats to loot the village. The self-defense corps killed six bandits. The bandit leader then ordered the village to be set on fire from all sides. The village was immediately engulfed in flames, and the residents fled in panic. Unfortunately, the village was surrounded by water, and many residents drowned. The bandits also shot and killed over thirty people. By 9:00 PM, all the bandits had left. Out of three hundred households, two hundred and fifty-four were burned down. Over thirty people were burned to death, and two hundred and sixteen drowned people were recovered by neighboring villages. The number of people missing and unaccounted for is estimated to be between one hundred and forty and one hundred and fifty. This is a truly unprecedented disaster.

Red Pill Factory Uncovered 130

(Haimen) Chen Shicai, of Fuyin Township in the Sixth District, secretly established a factory to manufacture red pills, which he transported and sold in the Xisha area for huge profits. Several days ago, someone secretly reported him to the county party headquarters. Special Agent Cao led a team of security guards to search the premises, where they seized a bag of raw materials and two tins of red pills. Chen Shicai, the drug dealer, was arrested and sent to the county government. Yesterday, he was transferred to the Nantong District Security Command for interrogation.

Strictly Prohibit Deceitful People From Luring Farm Girls 131

(Nantong) Due to the drought-stricken harvest this year, the rural economy is in dire straits. Recently, unscrupulous people in Shanghai have been taking advantage of this situation, colluding with local thugs, using the pretext of recruiting female workers for major factories in Shanghai, luring unmarried girls aged sixteen to twenty from farming families, and transporting them to Shanghai to sell them. The Nantong District Administrative Inspector's Office has ordered the six counties to strictly investigate and prohibit this activity.

Agreed on Measures to Stabilize Rice Prices 132

(Jiaxing) The Jiaxing County Government, concerned about the soaring rice prices and their impact on the livelihoods of the poor, ordered rice merchants to raise 3,000 yuan to purchase rice for price stabilization. The subsidized sales was originally scheduled to begin on September 6, but because it was difficult to collect the funds, it was postponed until the other day. Then the Chamber of Commerce convened a meeting to discuss measures to stabilize rice prices, and the following was decided: (1) Appoint people to investigate poor households inside and outside the city and in the four suburban areas to provide them with subsidized purchase certificates, with a ten-day investigation period. (2) The consumption rate for sales should not exceed 5%. (3) The rice sold at subsidized prices should be purchased from Hunan. (4) The sales location should be at the Lanxi Guild Hall.

County Chamber of Commerce Cables to Protest the Abolition of Old Stamps 133

The Jiaxing County Chamber of Commerce stated that the Ministry of Finance's announcement to change the stamp tax, limiting the use of old stamps from the beginning of the issuance of the new stamps, has resulted in merchants' unused stamps being rendered worthless. It has cabled the Ministry of Finance to request that old stamps be allowed to be exchanged for new stamps within a limited time, in order to maintain national credit. At the same time, the Chamber of Commerce has sent telegrams to all cities and counties in the province to jointly advocate for this issue.

Shanghai City Today's Commemoration 134

(September 18th) The Third Anniversary Commemoration will be held at 10:00 AM. The entire city will fly flags at half-mast and observe a moment of silence to express grief. All entertainment venues will be closed. Mothers and apprentices commemorate by rising up. Today marks the anniversary of the unprovoked invasion of our Northeast by the brutal Japanese three years ago. All our compatriots, upon this national humiliation commemoration, are filled with indignation. The Central Government, to show our nation's determination to recover lost territory, has specially formulated commemorative measures. The City Party Department of this city has specifically followed regulations for citizen commemoration measures, publishing announcements in newspapers for public knowledge. In addition to separate commemorations by various organizations, groups, and schools, a commemorative meeting will be held at 10:00 AM today at the Youth Propaganda Corps, convening representatives from all walks of life. All entertainment venues in the city will be closed to express grief. The City Party Department will also issue a declaration to the public. Details are as follows:

(Today's Morning Commemorative Meeting) At 10:00 AM today, representatives from all walks of life in the city will hold a commemorative meeting at the Youth Propaganda Corps in Xiaoximen. The meeting staff was already seen in yesterday's newspaper. The venue was arranged properly last night. A Party-State flag and a white cloth banner with the words "(Shanghai City Representatives Hold (September 18th) Third Anniversary Commemorative Meeting)" were hung in front of the main entrance. A white cloth banner was also hung on the podium in the venue, with the Prime Minister's portrait and the Party-State flag in the center. Order slogans were posted on both sides, and slogans were pasted all over the walls. The scene was quite solemn.

(Commemorations by Institutions and Schools) In addition to the commemorative meeting convened by the City Party Department at the Youth Propaganda Corps, all institutions and groups in the city have received notices from the City Party Department to convene separate commemorative meetings. All schools have also received orders from the Ministry of Education, so today all institutions, groups, and schools are uniformly holding commemorations.

(Theaters, Dance Halls, and Restaurants Closed) Today is a National Humiliation Memorial Day. All those with a sense of honor will no longer indulge in scenes of wine, women, song, and dance. Therefore, after being notified by the City Party Department, the organizers of various entertainment venues also expressed deep sympathy and voluntarily closed their businesses for one day. Such as the Grand Stage, Samsung Stage, Tianchan Stage, and other theaters; Nanjing, Grand Light, Cathay, Grand Shanghai, Golden City, Beijing, and other cinemas; Grand East, Metropolis, East Asia, Yangtze, Lafayette, Grand Shanghai, Grand China, and other dance halls; Wei Ya, Nanyuan, New Asia, YMCA, Zhimeilou, Yuebinlou, East Asia, Grand East, New New, Atlantic, and other restaurants and taverns; Grand World, New World, Small World, and other amusement parks, are all closed for one day. All major and small newspapers will also cease publishing entertainment news and advertisements.

(Half-Mast Flags to Express Grief, Strict Vigilance) Today, all organs, groups, schools, party headquarters at all levels, business firms along the roads, and residents in the city all followed the notification of the City Party Department and flew flags at half-mast to express grief. The Songhu Garrison Headquarters, the Municipal Security Office, and the Public Security Bureau, in order to prevent reactionary elements from taking the opportunity to cause trouble, specifically ordered their subordinate districts, offices, and teams to increase posts at sentry points, and also ordered supervisors, detectives, male and female inspectors to work with police officers from various districts and offices to strictly check pedestrians. At the junction of the Chinese and foreign concessions, such as the North Sichuan Road area, special stringent precautions were taken. The police authorities of the two concessions also separately ordered the police stations to send more detectives to prevent disturbances in earnest.

(Measures for Commemoration by All Citizens) To oppose the atrocities of Japanese imperialism, all residents will fly flags at half-mast today, wear black gauze armbands, stop working for five minutes starting at 11:00 AM, stand up to commemorate, vow to avenge national humiliation, and offer deep condolences to the soldiers who died resisting Japan and the compatriots who were martyred. At the same time, stop all entertainment and recreation, and do not participate in any banquets, to express mourning. (Today's Mail Stamped with Commemorative Mark) Today, all mail passing through the Shanghai Postal Bureau will be specially stamped with a commemorative postal mark to commemorate the brutal Japanese invasion of the Northeast without cause. It is said that this measure has already been properly coordinated by the City Party Department and the Postal Workers' Union, so today's packages and letters will all have this commemorative stamp.

(City Party Department Issues Declaration to the Public) Declaration to the Public on the Third Anniversary of September 18th: Dear compatriots, today is the unprecedented September 18th National Humiliation Commemoration for our nation. Recalling this day three years ago, the Japanese imperialists, wielding their gunboat policy like a stroke of madness, began to invade our Northeast Shenyang. Within a morning, they seized more than a dozen cities such as Changchun and Yingkou. Within two months, they captured the three northeastern provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang. Then they invaded our Songhu, disturbed our Pingjin, occupied our Rehe, and established puppet organizations. Thus, more than four million square miles of our territory and more than thirty million of our compatriots were all under their iron hooves. Is this unprecedented and tragic national humiliation not a deep hatred and great insult to our entire nation? Since September 18th, on the part of our government, we have sought peace externally and examined national strength internally, not hesitating to endure humiliation and bear heavy burdens, first with appeals to the League of Nations, then with armed resistance. Although we have not been able to immediately return to the invaded land, we have inflicted a heavy blow on the brutal Japanese in spirit. On the part of our people, all are filled with righteous indignation. On the front lines, they organized volunteer armies, raised banners, and went to justice to resist the stubborn enemies. In the rear, they vigorously implemented boycott movements, causing a great blow to the brutal Japanese industry and commerce. What is regrettable is that not long after, the powerless League of Nations could not subdue the brutal Japanese, and our bodies of flesh and blood could not match the sharpness of their planes and guns, and our people's boycott movement also slackened over time. As a result, the brutal Japanese became even more unscrupulous, and the future consequences are truly unknown. Therefore, when we commemorate national humiliation today, we should learn from past mistakes, bury ourselves in hard work. First, we must know that if we want to control the fate of the brutal Japanese, there is nothing better than not buying Japanese goods, promoting domestic goods, and striving for thoroughness. Therefore, the boycott movement should continue to advance. Second, if we want to avenge national humiliation, we must first strengthen national power, and national defense construction is especially needed. Aviation is the key to national defense. Our compatriots must assist the government to complete the mission of saving the country through aviation. Third, the Red Bandits are a problem in our heart. To resist foreign aggression, we must first settle internal affairs. Our compatriots must first assist the government in completing the work of suppressing bandits in preparation for resisting Japan. In short, today, internal troubles and foreign invasions, the national crisis is no less than it was three years ago. Our compatriots should be aware that the country may be lost at any time, make the determination to rescue the dying and support the injured, embrace the spirit of lying on firewood and tasting gall, exert vigorous efforts, and work together. Only then can lost territory be recovered and national hatred avenged. I am willing to encourage this with my compatriots. Shanghai Special City Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang.

(Wang Delin's Anti-Japanese Battle Achievements) After the four northeastern provinces were invaded and occupied by the Japanese invaders, the destruction and trampling were meticulous. However, volunteer armies in various places still fought and fought with them from time to time. During the year, the period of green gauze tents was the most active. The General Headquarters of the Northeast Volunteer Army sent Adjutant Xu Yuanshun, who traveled south from Shanhaiguan, to report that the department had engaged in 40 or 50 large and small anti-Japanese battles between June, July and August. The greatest achievements are outlined below: (1) Wu Yicheng fought to the death in Luozigou. Wu Yicheng, the commander-in-chief of the Northeast Volunteer Army, was brave and good at fighting and had a long-standing reputation. At the end of July, Wu led hundreds of troops to attack Luozigou in Dunhua. When it was captured, the Japanese and puppet troops gathered a large force and surrounded them. Wu desperately fought the trenches for several hours, but eventually it was difficult to defend due to the fierce artillery fire, so he broke through the encirclement and escaped. In this battle, Wu's department lost more than 100 officers and soldiers, and the enemy also suffered significant losses. (2) Kong Xianrong fought steadily and calmly at the front, and had both courage and strategy. He was known as Little Kongming. Recently, he has been running around on the north and south sides of the Middle East Road. Most of his direct departments are in the Mishan and Ning'an areas. Hengdaohezi, the Middle East Road, is the most important station in the middle section. In early August, Kong led his troops into the station twice, overturned his grain trucks, and forced the Japanese soldiers escorting the trucks to disarm, but he did not harm them. Therefore, the Japanese soldiers mostly felt his benevolence and feared his prestige. (3) Zhang Yuting showed his magical powers by destroying roads in Yimianpo. Zhang Yuting, the director of the department, is a blood-spirited and brave general. In recent years, he has been guerrillas with Japanese and puppet troops in the mountainous areas such as Dengshahe and Yimianpo in the western section of the Middle East Road. He has made remarkable achievements. Recently, he specializes in destroying railway traffic. Few eastbound bullet trains or grain trains passing through here are spared. In mid-August, on one occasion, in order to avoid the eyes and ears of the rebels, the Japanese army drove at night with a full load of ammunition and 100 police officers to protect it. However, when approaching a certain mountain in Yimianpo, the car was overturned again, and the ambush troops on both sides rose up and killed dozens of Japanese soldiers. His methods were so quick that they shocked the Japanese. Recently, Yi Army was suspected of being instigated by the Soviet Russia, or even by the Communist Party, which is nothing more than being paranoid.

(Anti-Japanese Heroes Escaped Danger and Returned South) Peace News Agency Special Report, Tian Zhongyi, a native of Changzhou, Jiangsu, was a teacher at Peizi Middle School in Shenyang, Northeast. During the (September 18th) campaign, he hated the barbarity of the brutal Japanese and could not bear the fall of the territory. He immediately joined Xiaobailong's department and served as the benevolence team. Xiaobailong's department was divided into three teams: wisdom, benevolence, and courage. The volunteer army fought against the Japanese Kou many times, taking the lead and killing countless enemies. Unfortunately, during the plot to seize Shenyang City last winter, he was captured by the Japanese army and suffered severe torture. The Japanese were inhumane and used sharp small knives to cut Tian's pupils into a cross shape. Then, they injected alkali into the eye sockets, causing Tian's eyes to become blind instantly. Fortunately, this spring, our volunteer army rescued Tian from danger. After escaping danger, Tian endured hardship and begged for food along the way to return south. He arrived in Ningbo on the 16th of this month and planned to take a bus to the Hangzhou Security Office to find his brother, who was a company commander in a certain regiment of the Security Team. Because he had no money, he wandered around the Yong Station. Later, a certain passenger gave him a third-class ticket, and Tian took the train leaving Yong for Hangzhou at 1:55 p.m. The Yong reporter of the Peace News Agency, because it was reported that Xiaobailong had lost his honor and surrendered to the enemy, once asked Tian about this matter. According to Tian, Xiaobailong's department was scattered in all directions, and there were still more than 20,000 people. Xiaobailong himself, due to insufficient support, temporarily hid in the mountains and forests. The rumors of his loss of honor were by enemies and were by no means true.

(China Merchants Public Bus Mourns) Shanghai China Merchants Public Bus Company held a memorial ceremony on September 18th. The following is the announcement method obtained by the company: For announcement purposes, it is verified that September 18th is the traumatic event of the fall of our Northeast. The memorial on that day is a national mourning. It has been seen in the newspaper that the order has been issued. Our company is owned by the Chinese people and must sincerely comply with it. It is decided that from 11:00 a.m. on that day, all employees should follow orders to stop working for five minutes and stand up to mourn to express the national crisis. The memorial method is listed below. All employees must follow it. (1) Flags should be flown at half-mast inside the company and on all vehicles in operation. (2) Regardless of whether the vehicle is in operation or not, it must stop working for five minutes. (3) When the vehicle is in operation, the driver must park the car on the side of the road on time for memorial services. If passengers in the car do not understand, the ticket seller should calmly state it. (4) If the car is parked at the terminal station, all staff members must use the whistle as a sign (stop work immediately when the whistle sounds randomly and completely, and resume seven actions after the whistle blows for a long time). The whistle is the responsibility of the timekeeper. (5) In the company factory and writing room, the guide clock is used to mourn silently, that is (stop work when the bell rings randomly, and start to stand up to mourn. After the bell rings once, start work). The bell is the responsibility of the car staff. (6) For the sake of mutual mourning, all staff members must wear black gauze armbands on that day (black gauze is prepared and issued by the company and can be collected from the car affairs and general affairs departments).

Zhejiang Autumn Cocoon Loan of 3 Million Yuan 137

Fourteen Banks Borrow

A Draft Agreement Has Been Agreed Upon

Guowen News Agency reports that Zeng Yangpu, Director of the Zhejiang Construction Department, has specially designated 900,000 yuan of Zhejiang Province silk cocoon and local company bonds as collateral to borrow 3 million yuan from 14 banks in Shanghai for the purchase of Zhejiang Province autumn cocoons, silk reeling, and transportation. Mr. Zeng came to Shanghai to negotiate with the banking group. The details are as follows:

(Fourteen Banks Borrow Funds) The banks borrowing the Zhejiang autumn cocoon loan this time include China, Transportation, Zhejiang Industrial, Shanghai Commercial, Zhongnan, China, Industrial, Jincheng, Salt Industry, Mainland, China National Goods, Zhejiang Industrial, China Communications, China Reclamation, Siming, and other 14 organizations (a Zhejiang silk cocoon loan banking group). (The previous report that the Central Bank and the China Bank jointly borrowed 1.5 million yuan was a misreport, because the Central Bank did not join). Among the 14 banks, China, Transportation, and Zhejiang Industrial were promoted as representatives of the banking group.

(Mr. Zeng Yangpu Came to Shanghai for Negotiations) Mr. Zeng Yangpu first contacted the Hangzhou branch of the Bank of China. After a clue, he came to Shanghai from Hangzhou with Mr. Shou Jingwei the day before yesterday to make separate contacts, and once invited bank representatives to a banquet to facilitate the progress.

(Meeting Held Yesterday to Revise the Contract) At 2:00 p.m. yesterday, Mr. Zeng borrowed the hall of the Bank Association on Hong Kong Road again and invited representatives of various banks to discuss the contract. Those present included Ye Fuxiao from the Mainland Bank, Chen Zheqing from the Salt Industry Bank, Ye Zhuotang from the Siming Bank,

Page 14

Shou Yicheng from the Bank of China, Zhang Peishen from the Bank of Communications, Zou Bingwen from the Shanghai Bank, Zhu Sensheng from the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Chen Duoru from the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, and more than a dozen others. Some improvements were made to the borrowing method, purpose, interest, repayment, and management.

(Draft Agreement to Be Signed Today) The draft agreement prepared at yesterday's meeting is roughly as follows: Loan contract, because the Zhejiang Provincial Government is implementing control, promoting production, improving silk cocoons, and relieving drought, it is agreed by both parties to borrow 3 million yuan of national currency from China, Transportation, Zhejiang Industrial, Shanghai Commercial, Zhongnan, China Industrial, Jincheng, Salt Industry, Mainland, China National Goods, Zhejiang Industrial, China Communications, China Reclamation, Siming and other banks. The important terms are as follows: (1) This loan shall be borne by the Bank of China for 750,000 yuan, the Bank of Communications for 450,000 yuan, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank for 400,000 yuan, the Shanghai Commercial Savings Bank for 300,000 yuan, Zhongnan and China Industrial each for 150,000 yuan, Jincheng, Salt Industry, Mainland, China National Goods, Zhejiang Industrial, China Communications, China Reclamation, and Siming eight banks each for 100,000 yuan, totaling 3 million yuan, which will be allocated in installments according to the provincial government's plan. (2) This loan is limited to the cost of purchasing this year's Zhejiang autumn cocoons, silk reeling, and transportation. (3) The interest on this loan is set at 1% per annum. (4) This loan is secured by silk cocoons and local government bonds with a par value of 900,000 yuan. (5) The banking group may send personnel to audit. (6) The repayment period is eight months. It is heard that it can be signed today.

Shanghai Port Authority Ordered Automatic Dredger from Germany 138

Launching Ceremony at German Bank on the 15th

It Can Sail to China in March Next Year

Wang Jingshun, secretary of the Shanghai Port Authority, told a reporter from the East China News Agency that foreign ocean-going ships must pass through the East China Sea to enter the Wusongkou and the Huangpu River. Between the East China Sea and the Huangpu River, there is a place called Shentan. The water in this shoal is shallow, and all larger ships must wait for high tide before they can enter the port. If there is no high tide, they will anchor immediately. Director Song Ziliang of this bureau, in order to

Dredge the Shoal to Facilitate Traffic, Ordered an Automatic Dredger from the Danzig Shipyard in Germany. The ship is named (Construction). This ship is the largest dredger in the world.

The Contract for Ordering this Ship was Signed in Germany last winter after being witnessed by our Minister to Germany, Liu Wendao. After Minister Liu sent the contract to China for review, the keel was laid in the Danzig Shipyard. The bureau specifically sent Engineer Smith of the Dredging Department and Assistant Engineer Zhu Chongxi to the factory to supervise the construction. The external hull of the ship has been completed. Yesterday, the Port Authority received a telegram from our Minister to Germany, Liu Chongjie, stating that the (Construction) dredger, etc., were in the Danzig Shipyard dock

Hold a Launching Ceremony at 2:00 p.m. on the 15th of this month. Mrs. Liu, wife of the Minister, broke the bottle, and all members of the Chinese Embassy in Germany attended the ceremony. The director of the shipyard delivered a speech, and Minister Liu gave a reply (the text is omitted). They raised champagne to celebrate the completion. The cost of this ship is £1,500,800. This amount must be

Pay in Installments until the entire ship is completed and sailed to China. After the test run matches the signed contract and is deemed satisfactory, the entire cost will be paid off. If the dredging is less than eight-tenths of the original contract, it can be returned in full. According to Mr. Wang, the ship is automatic. While sailing, it dredges itself. Every ten hours, it can dredge 30,000 tons of mud. After the mud is full, there is also machinery that can automatically release it. The construction is very ingenious. The ship is 360 feet long, 60 feet wide, and the draft is 18 feet when fully loaded. The entire project is expected to be completed in about February next year, and the two engineers of this bureau who were sent to Germany to supervise the construction will

Supervise the Arrival in China in March. After arriving in China and the test run is successful, it will be officially accepted and sailed to the Shentan waters of the Yangtze River in the East China Sea to start dredging work. If the results are good, another ship will be added to the factory so that both parties can operate one ship at a time.

China Merchants Bureau Opens Overseas Shipping Routes 139

Pooan Steamer to Set Sail for Little Luzon

Regular Service to Begin in November

The China Merchants Bureau has commissioned the construction of four new seagoing vessels in England: the Haiyuan, which left England on the 14th of this month and is expected to arrive in Shanghai on October 19th; the Haiheng, scheduled for November; and the Haizhen and Haili, both expected to arrive in December. The Bureau has decided on the routes for these four new ships, with three to operate on the Qingdao-Shanghai and Swatow-Hong Kong-Guangdong lines, and the other to sail the Shanghai-Qingdao-Yantai-Tianjin northern route. With these four ships in service, the number of sailings between Shanghai and Qingdao will be abundant. The existing Pooan steamer will then be difficult to continue on that route. The Bureau has therefore resolved to redeploy the Pooan to overseas routes, in order to develop shipping in Southeast Asia.

(Designated Special Vessel) To develop shipping to the South Seas Islands with Chinese vessels, the Bureau has conducted a thorough investigation. Between Xiamen and Little Luzon, there are over 100,000 overseas Chinese traveling each year. Overseas Chinese in the Philippines have repeatedly requested that the China Merchants Bureau dispatch ships to operate on this route, in order to reclaim commercial interests. The Bureau has now decided to reassign the Pooan steamer to the Xiamen-Philippines route, as its passenger capacity makes it ideal for this service. After several days of discussion, the business department has already begun planning the procedures for commencing service, and projecting the revenue and expenditure of the business.

(Overseas Compatriots Welcome) Many of the overseas Chinese in Manila and other places are natives of Fujian and Guangdong. Every year, over a thousand people travel between these places and the homeland, taking ships from Xiamen. Currently, the only passenger ship operating on this route is the British Taikoo Company's Anqing, with a displacement of over 3,400 tons. Fares are very high and business is booming, with first-class cabins costing one hundred yuan, second-class eighty-two yuan, and third-class over sixty yuan. Even steerage costs more than thirty yuan. Each year, overseas Chinese money leaks into foreign ships to the tune of hundreds of thousands of yuan. They have repeatedly requested that the China Merchants Bureau send ships to operate this service, both to relieve the oppression of overseas Chinese and to reclaim commercial interests. Now, upon hearing that the Pooan steamer will open a Xiamen-Philippines service, overseas Chinese in Manila have expressed extreme welcome, and those in the Philippines are willing to assist with all their strength. The Pooan steamer, once preparations are complete, is scheduled to officially begin service in early November.

Gold Exchange to Use Customs Gold Standard Starting Yesterday by Order of the Ministry 140

After the Ministry of Finance banned margin trading speculation, the Gold Exchange was ordered to comply and submitted a request through the supervisor to the Ministry for an extension. The Ministry approved the extension, but stipulated that no new transactions could be made during the extension period. From October 16th, the Customs Gold Unit issued by the Central Bank would be used as the delivery standard. The Exchange immediately convened a meeting of brokers, who resolved to comply. Starting yesterday, all December transactions made at the Exchange would use the Shanghai Central Bank Gold Price, that is, Customs Gold, as the standard.
