Five Medical and Pharmaceutical Groups to Commemorate Renowned Doctor Zhu Rongjing 143

Mr. Zhu Rongjing, a renowned doctor from Shanghai, was skilled in scientific medicine, poetry, and painting, and was one of the talents of recent times. Early in his life, he was appreciated by Mr. Li Youzhi, a renowned master of this town. As a young man, he studied in Japan and graduated from Nagasaki Medical University. During the Xinhai Revolution, he worked for the Red Cross and made great contributions. In the fourth year of the Republic, he taught at the Suzhou Provincial Medical University with enthusiasm, and his students were numerous. In recent years, he practiced medicine in southern Shanghai, saving countless people with his benevolence. He also devoted himself to public service, serving as a director and supervisor in various medical and pharmaceutical groups. In his spare time, he indulged in poetry and wine, forming literary societies with close friends and composing poems almost every evening. Such was his elegant taste. Unfortunately, he suddenly passed away on the 18th of last month due to a cerebral hemorrhage, causing universal lament. The Medical and Pharmaceutical Society of the Republic of China, the Shanghai Physicians Association, and the New Asia Pharmaceutical Factory, among other five groups, will hold a memorial service at 1:00 PM on the 23rd of this month (Sunday) at No. 119 Xiaozha Bridge Road outside Xiaonanmen. House Collapses in Heavy Rain in Yangjing, Injuring Two 148

Cheng Hu's Entire Family Fortunately Escapes

In Gaojia Alley, West of Yangjing Town in Pudong, there are three courtyards of old houses facing west, all inhabited by the Gao family. It is said that their ancestors were officials in the Ming Dynasty, and the house has been built for three hundred years, so it is extremely dilapidated. In recent days, due to the heavy rain, the walls, pillars, and roofs are all soaked in rainwater, and the seven bays of the building are unable to bear the pressure and are gradually becoming difficult to support. At 4:10 PM yesterday, a cracking sound was heard. The eight or nine families living in these seven old houses were startled and fled at the same time. Then, Gao Xu, the wife of the house owner Gao Baochun, and Gao Yu, the wife of Gao Miaogen, seeing that the house was unlikely to collapse for a while, risked entering to retrieve important objects. Suddenly, a sharp cracking sound was heard, and the seven bungalows completely collapsed. Xu and Yu were unable to escape and were crushed under the tiles. The nearby police station immediately reported to the third district and third year, and Director Jiang ordered the police to overturn the collapsed house and rescue the two women. Xu was found to be bleeding from the head, and Yu was found to have injured her abdomen. It was determined that Xu was old and weak and could not last long, while Yu was young and strong, but her injuries were serious. They were immediately ordered to be sent to the Pudong Hospital for treatment. A report was also submitted to the Public Security Bureau for verification. Before the collapse of the house, a strange thing happened. It is said that a Chongming native named Cheng Hu, who rented a house in the house, had a family of seven, old and young. Yesterday morning, Cheng Hu's wife suddenly saw the paper statue of the kitchen god being blown by the wind, with its face facing inward, which she thought was unlucky. Therefore, in the morning, the whole family moved to No. 8 Youfang Alley in the east. Unexpectedly, the house collapsed that afternoon, so Cheng Hu's family all raised their hands to celebrate.

So, she persuaded Hu to prepare more travel expenses and let her accompany her mother back home. Hu initially had no objections. Ma then knew that Hu was definitely malicious in abandoning her. She immediately took her mother and child and moved elsewhere. On one hand, she hired lawyer Zhu Honglie to file a criminal complaint with the First Special District Local Court against Hu, requesting that he be punished for abandonment in accordance with Article 309 of the Criminal Law, and filed a civil lawsuit, requesting that the defendant pay alimony of three thousand yuan at once. He was sent to the court, but due to insufficient evidence, he was acquitted. However, Ren had committed many crimes in his hometown, so he was temporarily detained in the civil detention center to await further action. Fang and Wu were returned to custody.

Handgun and Bullets Seized on Trolleybus 164

Zhang Rongbao Arrested On the Spot

Chen Qiaosheng Flees Alertly

At 10:20 AM on the 15th of this month, a Route 16 trolleybus was passing the intersection of Macgregor Road and Gordon Road. Officers No. 30 (Western officer) and No. 3137 (Chinese officer) from the Gordon Road police station were searching passengers and vehicles in the area. They boarded the trolleybus and searched it. In the third-class compartment, they found a newspaper on the floor under a seat. Underneath the newspaper was a handgun. They picked it up to inspect it, and found another handgun and two rows of bullets, totaling 18, underneath the newspaper. At that time, Zhang Rongbao, a native of Jiangyin, was standing next to the spot where the handguns were found, acting suspiciously. They arrested Zhang and took him, along with the guns and bullets, to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Eighth Criminal Division of the First Special Court. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin prosecuted him under Article 200 of the Criminal Code for endangering public safety and Article 1 of the Regulations for the Suppression of Military Firearms. He stated that the defendant had confessed at the police station that on the 14th of this month, he met his friend Chen Qiaosheng at a teahouse on Shandong Road and agreed to go to Caojiadu on Jessfield Road to collect a debt at 10:00 AM on the 15th. He met Chen on Fujian Road and then boarded a Route 16 trolleybus. When they passed Macgregor Road, Chen quickly threw the handguns under the seat and went to the first-class compartment. After being searched by the Chinese and Western officers, he got off the trolleybus and fled. The defendant tried to escape, but it was too late. Chen is still at large. He requested an extension. Judge Liu briefly questioned the defendant and ordered him to be detained for seven days for further investigation.

Shareholders Spoil the Fun, Manager's Conduct is Outrageous

Released on Bail During the Honeymoon Period; Case Adjourned for Further Investigation

Mei Shiwei (号 Jingfang), the 35-year-old manager of the Xinhua Silk Weaving Factory at 157 Route Conty, French Concession, is a native of Tiantai, Zhejiang Province. As a shareholder and manager, he joined with four and a half shares (valued at 100 yuan each) in the 15th year of the Republic. Despite only earning a salary of dozens of yuan per month, he lived lavishly and dressed extravagantly, arousing the suspicion of other shareholders. Recently, Mei, feeling lonely as his wife was in the countryside, was introduced to a woman in Shanghai and decided to take her as a concubine. He chose the Great World South Shou Dali Chun Shaoxing Restaurant as the venue for the wedding ceremony on the 15th and emptied the rooms upstairs in the factory, renovating them to serve as the new bridal chamber. This further aroused the attention of the shareholders. Shareholder Xu Jinfang (38 years old, from Tiantai) carefully examined Mei's account books over the years and discovered that Mei had embezzled over 1,700 yuan by the end of last year. This year, from the beginning to the present, he had secretly misappropriated another 1,100 yuan. Furthermore, a set of redwood furniture belonging to the factory had been moved out by Mei without permission, and its whereabouts were unknown. Xu reported this to the French police and requested an investigation. Detective Qian Yumin and officer Yin Baoke investigated and confirmed the facts. They went to arrest Mei on the morning of the 15th, on the auspicious day of his wedding. The wedding guests had arrived, but to their dismay, the groom was arrested, and the guests scattered. The detectives took the guest list (which had already recorded eleven wedding gifts) and more than ten account books from the factory as evidence to the police station. Yesterday, they were sent to the Second Special Court, where Judge Wu Fanglian presided over the hearing in the First Criminal Division. Police lawyer Fei Xizhen presented the case and requested a one-week extension to thoroughly investigate the case. Defendant's lawyer Jiang Yiping stated that the defendant was in the midst of his honeymoon and requested to be released on bail. The court ordered the case to be adjourned to the 21st for further investigation. The defendant was required to provide a surety of 3,000 yuan, or he would be detained.

Gao Anjun Killed While Defending Injustice 169

Intervening in a Dispute Over a Copper Coin, Humiliating a Thug

Gathering a Crowd for Revenge, One Bullet Fatal

Gao Anjun, a native of Shandong, 42 years old, formerly worked as a patrolman in the French police, assigned to the transportation department. He resigned due to failing eyesight. He lived with his wife, Gao Hu (40 years old, Anhui native), in the apartment above the garage at No. 183 Route Ladu, French Concession. A week ago, someone named Jia went to the Cheng Shuntai tobacco and paper shop opened by a woman, Cheng Gu, at No. 132 Rue Conty and bought a pack of cigarettes. He gave a two-jiao coin, and there was a dispute over the exchange rate of 480 wen versus 470 wen, a difference of one copper coin. Gao happened to pass by the shop and intervened, helping the shop and subduing Jia. After being dispersed by others, Jia left, humiliated and dissatisfied. Yesterday at 12:20 PM, he gathered several thugs to seek revenge on Gao. Gao was at home and resisted. Jia pulled out a handgun and fired at Gao, hitting Gao's left rib and exiting through his back. Gao fell to the ground, injured. The perpetrators fled. Patrolmen reported this to the police station on Rue Massenet. Gao was taken to Guangci Hospital, but due to the severity of his injuries, he died at 4:15 PM. The Western police chief ordered the detectives to investigate and arrest the perpetrators.

Wang Liubao and Others Take Revenge for Old Grudges

Yi Qingzhi Seriously Injured

Yi Qingzhi, 24 years old, from Beidongtai, was a night soil collector residing at No. 96, Dafu Lane, inside Dadongmen. Recently, for some unknown reason, he had a deep feud with his colleagues and fellow townsmen Wang Liubao (20 years old) and Xu Renyou (31 years old). Yesterday at around 3:00 PM, Yi went out and passed the entrance of Pinhua Fang on Anren Street inside Xiaodongmen. He was suddenly ambushed by Wang and Xu, who were lying in wait. They grabbed him and stabbed him repeatedly with three-inch knives. Yi was caught off guard and was stabbed more than ten times in the head, arms, legs, abdomen, and scrotum. Blood spurted from the wounds, and he fell to the ground, unconscious. Wang and Xu were covered in blood and tried to abandon the murder weapons and flee. Wu Guangzhen, a guard from the 24th post, heard the commotion and rushed over, arresting the two assailants and taking them, along with the two murder weapons, to the Second Precinct of the First District. Liu, the station chief, questioned them. Wang Liubao confessed that he lived at No. 82, Tiandeng Lane, Xiaonanmen. Yi, disregarding their relationship as colleagues and fellow townsmen, had extorted 15 yuan from his father on the pretext of being from Xiaojiangyin, and this was the reason for the attack. Xu Renyou's confession was the same as Wang's. Because the matter involved assault, they were ordered to prepare a document and send them to the police bureau for interrogation.

Old Woman Dies in Tragic Accident After Recovery 171

Gasoline Leaks From Container on Rickshaw,

Flames Ignite, Burns Prove Fatal

An elderly woman, Qi Qian, 66 years old, from Wuxi, came to Shanghai last month to visit her daughter, who was married to a Mr. Xu and lived at No. 4 Caojiadu. The old woman unexpectedly fell ill at her son-in-law's house. Her son, Qi Shengmao, a farmer in Wuxi, was too busy to come to Shanghai, so he sent his 18-year-old daughter to Shanghai to see her grandmother and bring medicine. Recently, the old woman's illness gradually improved, and she decided to return home. On the evening of the 13th of this month, she said goodbye to her daughter and son-in-law and hired a rickshaw with her granddaughter to go to the North Railway Station to take the train back to Wuxi. On the way, the stopper of a gasoline bottle (presumably for a primus stove) stored in a basket on the rickshaw came loose. The basket shook as the rickshaw puller ran, causing the bottle to tip over and leak gasoline. Some of the gasoline dripped onto the rickshaw lamp, causing a sudden burst of flames. The old woman's granddaughter jumped off the rickshaw and was unharmed. The old woman, due to her age and slowness, was caught in the flames. Her clothes and body were burned. The rickshaw puller stopped the rickshaw and extinguished the flames, but the old woman had already been severely burned. The Jing'an Temple police station was notified and sent Detective Qian Xianting to take the injured woman to Guangren Hospital for treatment. However, the elderly woman, having just recovered from an illness, was unable to survive the ordeal. She died from her injuries the day before yesterday. The police sent Detective Qian to take the body to the Fielun Road morgue. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Guo from the First Special District Court arrived at the morgue to examine the body and inquire about the incident. He ordered her son, Qi Shengmao, to sign a statement and take the body back for burial. The old woman ultimately died in a foreign land.

It has now been around for fourteen years, with gradual expansion. Since the addition of the dyeing department last year, it has been able to weave and process by itself, and the products have become more and more exquisite, and the business has become very prosperous. Yesterday, Chen Binghui and others, standing committee members of the Shanghai Citizens' Advocacy Association for Domestic Goods, together with Zhu Wenqi and others from the Silk Light Dyeing and Weaving Industry Association, drove to visit. After arriving at the factory, they were received by Manager Yan Guangdi and Factory Director Zhang Yunqi. The factory covers an area of ​​more than ten mu and has more than seventy new-style factory buildings with ample light and a large scale. Mr. Yan led them to visit the weaving department, which is divided into spinning, warping, and weaving departments. There were a total of 284 looms, all new automatic iron machines. Each female worker can manage two looms, divided into day and night shifts, and can weave more than 420 pieces of cloth. The factory's products are sold well in Guangdong, Fujian, and the Yangtze River provinces, especially in North China. All the representatives praised it as the most perfect domestic goods factory. After the visit, it was already five o'clock, and they all left.

Freight Training by the Two Railway Bureaus Commences Yesterday 178

The freight training course organized by the Jinghu (Beijing-Shanghai), Huhangyong (Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo) Railway Administration commenced its first session yesterday (the 17th). The venue was the night school classroom of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce at Tianhouguan Bridge. Around 9 a.m., representatives from various firms and factories arrived in the rain, totaling about forty people. First, Mr. Wu Shaozeng, the Deputy Director of the Railway Administration, delivered a speech, which lasted for half an hour. After a ten-minute break, Mr. Liu Dingxin, the Deputy Chief of the Traffic Department of the Railway Administration, instructed on the methods and key points of the group visits. Then, the training commenced according to the scheduled program. The main points of Deputy Director Wu's speech are recorded below. Economic relations in modern society can be considered extremely intricate, but in general, they are essentially

Page 16

the relationship between (supply) and (demand). When supply and demand are appropriately balanced, society is peaceful. When supply and demand are imbalanced, whether supply exceeds demand or demand exceeds supply, society experiences panic. How can we achieve an appropriate balance between supply and demand? The most crucial factor is transportation. Because producers must have convenient transportation to move their goods out, and sellers must have convenient transportation to market their goods and reach consumers. Therefore, to adjust the relationship between supply and demand, producers, transporters, and sellers must cooperate fully and closely. Railways are large-scale transportation organizations. For both transportation and sales, they are as closely linked as arms and cannot be separated. Therefore, our railway, in its role as a transporter, has repeatedly discussed cooperation methods with various industrial and commercial sectors. As a result, we have established a general outline for cooperation between production, transportation, and sales along the railway lines, serving as a basis for implementation. Among the cooperative matters to be undertaken by our railway, one item is: (assigning personnel to guide or handle freight procedures in areas with significant production and sales of goods). Regarding handling freight procedures, our railway has already established business offices at Jing'an Temple Road, Shiliupu (Sixteen Pups) in Shanghai, and Taiping Road in Nanjing to undertake this work. Regarding guiding freight procedures, although our railway has published regulations for everyone's reference, the sequence of procedures and the calculation of freight, especially the responsibilities of freight transport, are relatively complex, which may not be easily understood by everyone. Therefore, we have specially invited you all here for the traffic personnel to explain to you, so that you can fully understand and eliminate any misunderstandings. In addition to verbally explaining the freight procedures, we will also accompany you to visit the Shanghai North Station and the MacKen Road Station to gain a

clear understanding from firsthand observation. This can be said to be the first step, and an important step, in the cooperation between production, transportation, and sales. As for our railway's further facilities to assist merchants in handling freight, we plan to actively promote the following main points: (A) Adding business offices in the locations of major stations to facilitate merchants' contact; (B) Establishing freight agencies in the interior to serve as branch offices of the business offices, providing full convenience for the transport of goods in and out of the interior; (C) Starting from next year, implementing the "business officeization" of all stations along the line, i.e., entrusting each station to handle the main work performed by the business offices. The purpose of this is to make the organization of our railway's freight transport system like the body commanding the arms, and the arms commanding the fingers, with a consistent system, achieving lively results. It is also hoped that cooperation between production, sales, and transportation can therefore be further realized from ideals to gradual reality. Next, let me talk about our future hopes. In the United States, there is something called a Traffic Club, which is a joint organization of shippers and carriers. If shippers have unclear points or difficulties, they can ask carriers to explain or help. Conversely, if carriers need the assistance of shippers, they can also discuss it. This kind of organization is truly the best method of cooperation. In the United States, there is also something called a Shippers Advisory Board,

which is entirely organized by shippers. Whenever there are issues of dissatisfaction with transportation organizations or hopes for improvement, the committee will jointly study and propose opinions to the transportation organizations. This kind of method, which can eliminate misunderstandings between the two parties, is also the best example of cooperation. This time, our railway's invitation to merchants to explain freight procedures, although it does not have the formal organization like that in the United States, also contains a part of the same function. It is hoped that in addition to studying freight procedures, everyone will raise questions and contribute opinions as much as possible in order to jointly improve transportation services. This would be most fortunate. That concludes my speech.

The illustrations include a seven-color cover of the beautiful mermaid Yang Xiuqiong, a map of Shanghai's new construction, eight pictures of Shanghai's summer children's health camp, a large three-color nude by Fang Xuegu, two two-color pictures of fitness taken by Chen Jinshi, thirteen current affairs photographs, seventeen pictures of the swimming craze, twelve pictures of recent events of the time, four Chinese paintings by Xie Zhiguang, eight photographs of Mount Lu, seven pictures of Shanghai's nurseries, three Crystal Palace designs, fourteen pictures of mountain climbing, five pictures of science and inventions, and six pictures of Hua Mulan's Jade Hairpin Hatred. Each of the twelve Chinese female stars by famous photographers Lang Jingshan, Chen Jia Zhen, Yan Ciping, and others, each has one picture, which is particularly exquisite. Five new film stills, six Ni Yide painting exhibition works, two world sculptures, nine cartoons, and four woodcuts, and a Shanghai Friends cartoon are all printed using photogravure and copperplate printing. Each issue sells for only 30 cents, less than half of the cost. Annual subscription is 3.20 yuan. The next issue will be a special National Day issue, with double the length and materials. It is said that Shanghai Magazine Company is currently in a low-price period, and both retail purchases and subscriptions are discounted by 10%.

Calligraphy and Painting News 182

Calligrapher Zhang Dan'an Returns to Shanghai After Escaping the Heat. Zhang Dan'an, also known as Yinxiangguan Master, is from Wujin. He is learned and talented, excelling in poetry, calligraphy, and literature, and he has a peculiar addiction to writing. Since resigning from his post in the late Qing Dynasty, he has abandoned his official ambitions and devoted himself to studying calligraphy and rubbings, tracing back to the Zhou and Qin dynasties and pursuing the Jin and Tang dynasties, learning from Shi Ru and being able to uniquely obtain his sociality. He is almost proficient in all styles and his characters are wonderful. The legalists admire him and all recognize his deep skill. Since the beginning of summer, due to the oppressive heat, he went to Mount Lu to recuperate for more than a month at the invitation of a friend. Many people who wanted his calligraphy were politely declined. Now that the weather is cool, he has returned to Shanghai yesterday and is accepting commissions as usual. Couplets are charged only one yuan per sheet, screen strips are doubled. True, cursive, official, and seal scripts are all available. He also writes eulogies, mourning notices, sacrificial texts, epitaphs, portraits, elegiac couplets, happy couplets, poems, and all kinds of practical documents for social occasions at low prices and with quick delivery. Fellow practitioners who wish to exchange their works with Mr. Zhang are also welcome. Send letters to Asia East Bank, Tianjin Road, Shanghai.

Medical News 183

Opening of the First Branch of the Zhonghua Obstetrics Hospital. The Zhonghua Obstetrics Hospital on Zhonghua Road, Nanshi, near Tan Jia Lane, has been providing free childbirth services to poor women for two years, and its attentive service has long been praised by local people. Recently, due to the development of hospital affairs, it has specially established a first branch at the intersection of Donghuhong Road and Zhaofeng Road in Hongkou. It has hired more than a dozen well-known doctors to provide rotating day and night childbirth services. The opening ceremony of the branch was held yesterday. Obstetrics experts Cao Zhixin, Pan Haoru, Liu Quangong, Liu Shusen, Wang Qinnan, Gu Baoluo, Wang Jingyu, Ru Aiyun, etc., as well as various groups, organizations, schools, and local gentry, attended. There were many congratulatory speeches, making it a grand occasion for a time.

Weather Report 185

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 p.m. yesterday stated that Shandong and its surrounding areas are cloudy with winds from the north to the northeast, quite strong. The local area is overcast, turning cloudy, with slight showers and strong northeasterly winds. The middle reaches of the Yangtze River have winds from the northwest to the northeast. The East Sea is cloudy with rain everywhere and prevalent northeasterly winds. The weather in the southeast and east of Luzon is bad due to a hurricane moving northwest. At 2 p.m., the center of the first hurricane was within 120 miles of the intersection of 19 degrees north latitude and 133 degrees east longitude, remaining stationary or moving very slowly. The center of the second hurricane was within 320 miles of the intersection of 15 degrees north latitude and 129 degrees east longitude, moving northwest. The wind force of both hurricanes is unknown. Also, in the 24 hours before 3 p.m. yesterday, the temperature in this port was 80.4 degrees at its highest and 72.1 degrees at its lowest. On the same day last year, the highest was 82.2 degrees and the lowest was 65.8 degrees.

Special Article

My Questions Regarding Governor Clementi's Speech at the British Malaya Society (Introduction) 187

Since Sir Clementi, after resigning as Governor of Hong Kong, took office as Governor of Singapore and High Commissioner of the Malay States in May 1929, his policy measures during the five years, in broad terms, include increasing national defense funds, decentralization, customs union, banning the Chinese Kuomintang, using Malay as the basis of education, promoting rice cultivation, rescuing rubber and tin, local industrialization, etc. His grand plans and ambitions, glaring at the Straits, the gains and losses of various policies, and their future impact are directly related to the political, military, and economic interests of the British colony. We do not need to overstep our authority to worry about it. Moreover, Sir Clementi, with his subjective views, before his resignation was approved, boasted of his achievements in governing Malaya on the platform of the United Kingdom, precisely to win public opinion in his country, which is not something we Chinese can interfere with. Only the matter of banning the activities of the Chinese Kuomintang is too far from the facts in his speech. We feel like a bone stuck in our throat on this issue and have wanted to say something about it for a long time. The authorities have not announced the reasons for the ban, and Singapore in the Straits Settlements is the hub of the three "S" lines. The British Empire regards it as an advanced important town to cope with the situation in the Pacific Ocean. More than 1.7 million overseas Chinese reside locally and in the Malay Federation, reclaiming wasteland and cultivating, prospering the land, with a long history and the most meritorious achievements. The intelligent British authorities should have no reason to discriminate against or despise them. At this time when the crisis in the Far East is becoming more apparent, Mr. Clementi received an important mission from the British Emperor, so we, based on the belief of coexistence and common prosperity, endured it and were unable to make a sudden discussion. Recently, Mr. Clementi raised six points against the Chinese Kuomintang in the United Kingdom, publicly pointing out the reasons. We now suddenly realized that the reasons he raised were nothing more than this. The British Emperor has approved Mr. Clementi's resignation, indicating that his policies and views may not necessarily represent the British government. Therefore, it increased our opportunity for discussion. We specially analyzed Mr. Clementi's various points based on objective facts and with a calm mind, so that people at home and abroad would know that Mr. Clementi does not yet have a full understanding of the Chinese Kuomintang and the Chinese nation.

(II) Historical Facts of the Chinese Kuomintang's Activities in Malaya 188

To discuss the issue of the Chinese Kuomintang's activities in British Malaya, we should briefly recall the past evolution of our party, because the activity process of all things has its own continuous relationship and is never formed out of thin air. Everyone knows that the predecessor of the Chinese Kuomintang was the Chinese Revolutionary Party, the Tongmenghui, and the Xingzhonghui. At first, the revolutionary patriots were motivated by national revolution because the Qing court went against the grain, humiliated the country, and forfeited its sovereignty, and saw that the various ethnic groups in the country were facing destruction. At that time, overseas Chinese, unable to bear the danger of their motherland, cried out loudly and received widespread support. They did their best to provide spiritual and material assistance for the revolution. The earliest organizations of the Triad Society in Singapore, Penang, Kuala Lumpur, Ipoh, Seremban, and other places, This kind of society began in the early Qing Dynasty and flourished in the late Qing Dynasty, with the purpose of restoring the Ming Dynasty and destroying the Qing Dynasty. Later, when Sun Yat-sen arrived in Nanyang (Southeast Asia), he connected with many patriots of different factions, such as the Yi Hing Association, Yi Fu Association, Fu Xing Association, Hai Shan Association, Guang Fu Association, and the parties who had successively lost the mainland and fled into exile after Zheng Chenggong and the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom, and conspired to restore the country. Therefore, overseas patriots followed Mr. Sun and joined the Tongmenghui. The patriotic overseas Chinese, contributing money and efforts, were even more prosperous for a time. Organizations like the Tongde Newspaper Society and Wanqing Garden in Singapore, the newly improved commercial firms in Kuala Lumpur and Ipoh, Juexing Garden, Civilized Pavilion, and the Xiaolan Pavilion and Guangyuan Reading Newspaper Society in Penang were all places where talents gathered. Branch associations in various places, such as Kuala Pilah, Seremban, Muar, etc., as well as distant places such as Yangon, the Dutch East Indies, Haiphong, and Siam, were filled with anti-Qing revolutionary comrades. After being changed to the Kuomintang in the first year of the Republic, a Kuomintang Transport Department was established in Singapore, and branch departments were established in various ports. After being changed to the Chinese Revolutionary Party three years later, the organization became even more grand. Although the Straits Settlements government had paid attention to it, legal requests for registration were made in the four Malay Federated States of Perak, Negeri Sembilan, Pahang, and Selangor, and permission was granted. It continued openly until 1925, a legitimate action without any harm to local security and order. Therefore, after being reorganized into the Chinese Kuomintang in 1924, in addition to the public party headquarters in the Malay Federation, it could still operate semi-publicly. During these decades, the party's general director, Mr. Zhongshan, and other important personnel of the party traveled and led in the Malayan region, and their comings and goings were extremely free. There was no obstacle to local famous overseas Chinese participating in the activities. The colonial authorities either watched coldly or secretly protected them. There has never been severe sanctions or dissolution. It was not until Mr. Clementi took office as Governor that the Chinese Kuomintang was labeled an illegal organization and banned. These historical facts can prove that the Kuomintang's activities did not hinder the resident government's intentions in the slightest. Moreover, the successive Governors of Singapore were not surprised by the Kuomintang's activities. It may not be that they were all less intelligent than Mr. Clementi. In fact, it was because Mr. Clementi ignored these historical facts that he could not help but be short-sighted.

(3) Mr. Kim's Six Points of Criticism and Questions for the Kuomintang 189

In his speech, Mr. Kim stated the following regarding the Kuomintang: "The Kuomintang's establishment in the Malay Peninsula contradicts local laws, yet it has openly operated since 1930, engaging in extensive political propaganda and encouraging local overseas Chinese, instilling anti-British sentiments in them. The Kuomintang's objectives in Malaya are:

(1) To organize all overseas Chinese in Malaya.

(2) To criticize laws that mistreat overseas Chinese.

(3) To invest in various agricultural, industrial, and commercial activities.

(4) To place all Chinese schools under party control.

(5) To compile school textbooks instilling anti-British ideas.

(6) To emulate Gandhi's non-cooperation movement, implementing non-cooperation between Malay Chinese and the government. Furthermore, they utilize Chinese newspapers as propaganda tools, subjecting newspaper owners to immense pressure, and labor employers face similar oppression. In summary, the purpose of the Chinese Kuomintang's Malayan branch is to undermine the loyalty of all local overseas Chinese to the British government..."

Regarding the first point, the phrase "organizing all overseas Chinese" is unclear. If it refers to "organization," it is neither notorious nor evil. The Kuomintang, being open and upright, would never stoop to bad organizations. Good "organizations," as mentioned above – such as Tongde Bookstore and Newspaper Agency, Wan Qing Yuan, Xin Gailiang Commercial Firm, Juexing Yuan, Wenming Ge, Xiao Lan Ting, Xin Guang Yuan, Reading Newspaper Agency, etc. – are mostly aimed at learning, public welfare, and loving the country. As for the existing overseas Chinese "organizations" – such as Chinese Chambers of Commerce in various places, various professional associations, Fujian, Guangfu, Chaozhou, Qiongzhou, Hakka associations, and San Yi, Si Yi, and county-based hometown associations and family groups, etc. – some are local in nature, others have clan significance, and all are for connecting feelings and strengthening kinship. They not only have no political function, but their establishment history predates the Kuomintang by decades or even centuries. In short, any overseas Chinese organization, new or old, must go through registration procedures with the local government before it can be established. Therefore, the phrase "organizing all overseas Chinese" is unclear whether it is a fabrication or based on reality. But examining ourselves from the perspective of the Kuomintang, we feel ashamed of our lack of such power. As for the overseas Chinese groups established before the Kuomintang, with their long history, how dare we claim their credit? The colonial government should have the wisdom to judge.

Regarding the second point, the phrase "criticizing laws that mistreat overseas Chinese," if the word "mistreat" is not a subconscious revelation by Mr. Kim himself, we would not dare to assert that the colonial government intends to mistreat overseas Chinese. Because the British Malayan government even has specialized agencies in the Straits Settlements to protect animals and prohibit any abuse. How could they not cherish the overseas Chinese, who are also human beings under their rule? Mr. Kim's mention of "mistreatment" only exposes his own shortcomings. The Kuomintang does not bear any guilt. The British monarch would surely be displeased upon hearing this. Whether mistreatment exists is a question. If there is no such thing at all, what is there for us to criticize? If it exists, not only would the Kuomintang pay attention, but also the dignified British rule of law would not allow it.

Regarding the third point, "investing in various agricultural, industrial, and commercial activities," we must ask whether the prosperity of Malaya is limited to investment by a certain type of person or a certain country. Are we overseas Chinese worthy of operating industries in Malaya? We cannot find such a basis in past history or current laws. Malaya, from its beginnings, went through years of struggle with nature to develop into today's prosperity. Everyone acknowledges that it was due to the cooperation of the intelligence, physical strength, and courage of overseas Chinese with the political power of the British colonial government. Furthermore, examining the migration of our overseas Chinese ancestors, not to mention those who went as far back as the Jin Dynasty, even Zheng He's seven voyages to Southeast Asia in the early 15th century placed his footsteps more than a hundred years ahead of Westerners. At that time, amidst miasma and thickets, where humans and beasts coexisted, overseas Chinese, with their adventurous nature, creative spirit, and hardworking perseverance, opened up a paradise for later generations with knives and axes. This is not our self-praise. Twenty years ago, Resident Ryan of Singapore said, "Before the arrival of white men in Malaya, Chinese were already mining, fishing, trading, and farming here. When white men arrived, they engaged in large-scale construction, relying entirely on the strength of Chinese. Administrative expenses and funds relied on this. Chinese who came here mostly went deep into the jungles to clear the wilderness, braving dangers for great profits. Although many died from heatstroke and miasma, they ultimately conquered nature, becoming workers, woodcutters, potters, and builders. Cultural and material construction both originated from them. They also invested heavily in organizing steamship companies to facilitate transportation, recruiting workers, and developing land resources, allowing the government to tax them, accounting for nine-tenths of the total local fiscal revenue..." More recently (last year), at the Kuala Lumpur Agricultural Exhibition, Mr. Kim, during his speech at the opening ceremony in front of a large crowd of overseas Chinese, earnestly advised residents to strive to develop agriculture, promote rice, tea, tobacco, and other industries, and to use Malayan products as raw materials for daily necessities, without seeking them afar, hoping that the local area could implement industrialization. He also prepared to purchase private properties in the western part of Singapore, under the jurisdiction of the Public Works Department, to develop factory areas, and the government would provide special accommodations for those willing to establish factories. From this, it can be seen that the contribution of overseas Chinese to the economic prosperity of Malaya in the past was so great, and the British government's current encouragement and rewards are also so generous. Therefore, investing in local industries is indeed beneficial to the livelihoods of the local people and enriches the government's coffers, benefiting both people and the land. Now, Mr. Kim criticizes overseas Chinese investment in industry in London, is this not a complete contradiction? How can this contradiction be explained? (To be continued)

Educational News

Recent Overview of Education in Nanjing City 190

The Nanjing City Social Affairs Bureau recently conducted a survey and statistics on the status of education in Nanjing in the 22nd year of the Republic. Now, with reference to the recent educational situation in Nanjing after the summer vacation, a summary is extracted and recorded below.

Educational Expenses: The recurring expenses of educational undertakings in Nanjing City are actually 57,503 yuan per month, which is divided into ten items: 1. First Middle School: 4,994 yuan; 2. Complete Primary Schools: 38,966 yuan; 3. Compulsory Primary Schools: 6,257 yuan; 4. Subsidies for Private Primary Schools: 934 yuan; 5. Vocational Supplementary Schools: 1,160 yuan; 6. Vocational Supplementary Schools for Women: 400 yuan; 7. School for the Blind and Deaf: 730 yuan; 8. Mass Education Schools: 2,153 yuan; 9. Municipal Library: 1,344 yuan; 10. Experimental Mass Education Center: 565 yuan.

Primary School Education: There are 39 municipal complete primary schools, with a total of 353 classes and 15,926 students (both male and female). There are 30 compulsory primary schools, with a total of 116 classes and 5,442 students (both male and female). After the summer vacation of the current 23rd year, in addition to merging the Kao Peng Primary School and Xinfuhe Primary School, several complete primary schools and compulsory primary schools will be added in Hankou Road, Shanxi Road, Jiulong Bridge, Jiangdongmen and other places. The number of additional classes is about 80. This is the situation of municipal primary schools. In addition, there are also the First and Second Traffic Workers' Children's Primary Schools in the capital, the Rotary Club of Pukou, the Rotary Club of Nanjing, the Children of Workers of the Jinling Arsenal, and the Children's School of the Capital Police, totaling 6 schools, 46 classes, and 1,603 students (both male and female). There are also the National Central University Experimental School and the two experimental primary schools of the Provincial Nanjing Middle School and Nanjing Women's Middle School, which belong to the scope of public, national and provincial schools. There are a total of 30 private primary schools that have been registered, with 109 classes and 4,365 students (both male and female). There are 16 schools with 63 classes and 1,958 students (both male and female) that have not yet completed the registration.

Kindergarten Education: 16 municipal schools have attached kindergartens, with a total of 888 children (both male and female). 5 private schools have attached kindergartens, with 240 children (both male and female). Number of Private Schools: Divided into 8 bureaus in the police station area, with a total of 574 schools and 14,995 students (12,054 males and 2,941 females).

Secondary School Education: There is only one municipal First Middle School, with 9 junior high school classes and 267 students (both male and female), 2 senior high school normal classes with 94 students (both male and female), and 3 senior high school general classes with 107 students (both male and female). There are 15 private middle schools that have been registered, with 75 junior high school classes and 3,245 students (both male and female), and 100 senior high school general classes with 2,138 students (both male and female). There are 8 schools that have not yet completed the registration procedures, with a total of 26 classes (1 senior high school class), and 954 students (both male and female).

Social Education: In the municipal area, in addition to schools for the blind and deaf, vocational supplementary schools, public libraries, experimental civil education centers, and civil education centers, swimming pools, public reading boards, popular lecture groups, drama review, vocational guidance, the Nanjing Literature and Nanjing Sports committees, etc., the Civil School has been open for 10 sessions. In the past, from the first to the ninth sessions, a total of 366 schools, 427 classes, 18,830 students and 10,657 graduates were held. In the 22nd year, there were 8 civil schools, and several schools attached with primary schools and compulsory primary schools. This year, after the summer vacation of the 12th session, one school will be added outside Hanximen Street and one school will be added in Xixiting, north of Dashugen inside Xuanwu Lake Gate. Together with the previous eight schools, there are a total of 10 schools. These are the ones established separately. There are 16 schools attached to simple primary schools and 10 schools attached to complete primary schools. In the private sector, there are 19 supplementary schools, with varying levels of primary and secondary schools. In addition to three or four schools with bookkeeping, typing, electricity, and pharmacy courses, the rest focus on knowledge subjects.

Vocational Education: The Qiwang Street Vocational Supplementary School and the Confucius Temple Women's Vocational Supplementary School, which were originally run in the city, did not have many vocational subjects. This year, they were reorganized after the summer vacation, focusing on vocational skills. The Qiwang Street Supplementary School has classes in civil engineering, Chinese typing, commercial advertising, and accounting (this class is held in the evening). The Confucius Temple Women's Supplementary School has been changed to a sewing class and a general housekeeping class. In addition, an infant care class has been established in Puyutang. This is currently a way to cope with poverty. After raising considerable funds, we will formally establish vocational schools. Previously, we planned to apply for Gengkuan subsidies to establish senior vocational schools, but due to the allocation of funds for this session, it was not mentioned. Therefore, not only can senior vocational schools not be established at present, but it is also difficult to establish junior vocational schools.

Cultural Groups: There are currently 48 cultural groups in Nanjing that have been approved or have reported to the Ministry of Education for record, including the Academic Research Association Resident Office in Nanjing, the Nanjing Library Association, the Capital Kindergarten Education Research Society, the Chinese Economic Society, the Chinese Agricultural Society, the Nanjing Branch of the Chinese Astronomical Society, the Chinese Forestry Society, the Secondary Arithmetic Research Society, the Chinese Children's Education Society, the National Mandarin Education Promotion Association, the New China Agricultural Society, the Chinese Sociological Society, the Chinese Metrology Society, the Nanjing Branch of the Chinese Art and Craft Society, the Chinese Mining and Metallurgical Engineering Society, the Chinese Testing Society, the Nanjing Calligraphy and Painting Research Society, the Chinese Political Science Society, the Chinese Scientific Movement Association, the Chinese Accounting and Political Society, the Chinese Chemical Society, the Fujian Students Association in Nanjing, the Chinese Medical Improvement Society, the New Education Research Society, the Nanjing Branch of the Chinese National Medicine Society, the Boy Scout Academic Research Society, the New Asia Society, the Chinese Political Economy Society, the Chinese Buddhist Society, the World Buddhist Society, the 19 Society, the Chinese Police Association, the Nanjing Irrigation Improvement Association, the Nanjing Amateur Sports Association, the Fourth North Cultural Itinerary of Mr. Strickland, British Cooperation Expert 191

The situation of Mr. Strickland, a British expert in cooperation, coming to China to give lectures has been recorded in previous reports. On the 15th, the Ministry of Education published the record of Mr. Strickland's itinerary as follows:

(A) (September to mid-November): (1) Stay in Nanjing for two weeks, contacting the Central Cultural Association, the National Economic Committee, the Central University, Jinling University, and the Agricultural Survey Institute of the Ministry of Industry; (2) Go to Wu Ping, Tianjin to Beiping to contact various groups and give lectures to various universities and research institutions. In Tianjin, contact Nankai University Economic Survey, etc. In Beiping, contact the China International Famine Relief Commission, etc.; (3) Travel to Shaanxi, from Beiping to Ding County to visit, and then go to Shaanxi to visit the cooperative work of the China International Famine Relief Commission; (4) From Shaanxi to Hankou, contact the Four Provinces Bank, return to Hankou, and take a boat to Nanjing; (B) (Mid-November to March 31, 1935): During this period, teach cooperative courses at Jinling University and give leadership lectures on special cooperative organizations to students from various ministries in China; (C) (April 1 to the end of June): Hold research seminars for the China International Famine Relief Commission, the Four Provinces Bank, and the National Economic Committee, and continue to study cooperatives and make brief reports.

Today is the 3rd anniversary of the September 18th Incident. In addition to inviting party members and celebrities to give speeches, the staff of the center will also perform a costume lecture ("Blood Sacrifice") to awaken the public and warn the public.

Chinese Science Society Edits Scientific National Renaissance 193

Observing the Chinese nation from a scientific perspective

Invite scholars to dedicate their research results to the people

The Chinese Science Society recently launched the editing of a book called "Scientific National Renaissance". The origin and content of the book are extracted as follows:

Origin: The poverty and weakness of our country today is well known. The way to save poverty lies in developing resources, and the way to save the weak lies in reorganizing the military and political affairs. These two can be realized in the short term. There is something even more important than this, that is, whether our nation itself has the ability to compete for survival. European and American countries regard us as an inferior nation, and our compatriots boast that we are an ancient country of culture and an excellent nation. With today's progress of science, this problem cannot be solved. Observing the Chinese nation from a scientific point of view and then deciding on the way to revive it is the purpose of this book. The country has already shouted for national revival, but most of them think from a political perspective. Our publication of this book is not to cater to the fashion, but to invite domestic scholars to contribute their research on various aspects of the nation, such as climate, food, and life expectancy, and tell the people of the country for reference in reviving the nation. Such research is often guided by scientists abroad, and many have actually implemented it politically. Even in terms of the descendants of idiots, Germany has strictly implemented it. The British capital has several states that implement it. In Germany, there will be 40,000 people who will be sterilized because they are rejected. The population of Germany is 62 million, so one in every 1,300 people will be sterilized. The precision of its selection is so great. There are more disabled and inferior people in our country than in Germany. Even in terms of the German ratio, at least 300,000 people in our country should undergo this operation, but our country has not paid attention to this. Thirty years later, the German nation will become more and more excellent, and our Chinese nation will become more and more inferior. What achievements can be said about cultural revival and cultural construction in this inferior nation? This is why we are so alarmed. There are many ways to revitalize the nation and improve the race through scientific methods. Food, education, and health are all dependent on the research of scientists. This book is not a prescription, but a stimulant. Domestic scientists are either concerned about this issue and have not completed their research, or they are concerned and have already achieved results. Therefore, we invite comrades to compile this book as a pioneer for the revitalization of the nation. This is also one of the ways our society serves China with science.

Content: Chapter 1: Historical Observation of the Chinese Nation; Chapter 2: Geographical Distribution of the Chinese Nation (led by Zhang Xiaofeng of National Central University); Chapter 3: Ancient Chinese Culture (led by Li Ji); Chapter 4: Northeastern Culture and the Chinese Nation (led by Ling Chunsheng); Chapter 5: Southwestern Chinese Culture (led by Liu Chongxi); Chapter 6: Climate and Chinese Culture (led by Zhu Kezhen); Chapter 7: Physiology of the Chinese Nation (led by Wu Taomin); Chapter 8: Physique of the Chinese Nation (led by Wu Junyi); Chapter 9: The Brain and Intelligence of the Chinese People (led by Lu Yudao); Chapter 10: Improvement of the Chinese Nation (led by Tao Yunkui); Chapter 11: Hygiene of the Chinese Nation (led by Yuan Yicheng); Chapter 12: Bloodline of the Chinese Nation (led by Li Chengpian); Chapter 13: Scientific National Renaissance. There are a total of 13 chapters and 130,000 words, with a period of six months.

Agricultural Expert Yu Hongzheng Returned from Japan Yesterday After Investigation 195

Japanese Agricultural Equipment is Extremely Simple

However, Japanese Scholars are Willing to Devote Themselves to Work

Professor Yu Hongzheng of Beiping University, an agricultural expert, was sent by the school to Japan to investigate agriculture a month ago. Now Mr. Yu has returned from Japan. A reporter from Guomin News Agency made a special visit. According to him, this trip to Japan was specifically for agricultural investigation, school equipment, and agricultural laboratory conditions. Generally speaking, Japanese agriculture has made considerable progress, but the simplicity of agricultural laboratory equipment is not as good as that of our country. However, the spirit of scholars' hard work and perseverance, and their dedication to work day and night, makes us infinitely admired. Although Chinese agricultural education has not made significant progress, in recent years, students who study agriculture have been willing to go deep into the countryside to work, which is indeed a good phenomenon. If we can persist in this for a long time, it is very hopeful for improving the future of agriculture. It is heard that Mr. Yu has decided to take the train back to Beiping today to draft an investigation report.

The Education Bureau will Issue Free Bullets for Live-Fire Shooting in All High Schools and Above 197

The Municipal Education Bureau yesterday instructed all public and registered private high schools, private universities, and private specialist schools that it was in accordance with the Ministry of Education's Order No. 09955, which opened the following: "It is approved by the Training Directorate General's dispatch, which opened the following: 'It is approved by the Ministry of Transportation's Army Weapons and Security Order No. 62, which opened the following: 'It is approved by your Ministry's Civilian Order No. 411, which opened the following: 'It is checked that Pan Youqiang, director of the National Military Education Department of this Ministry, was previously ordered to go to Jiangxi to report on the military training inspection and submitted a memorial to Chiang Kai-shek, chairman of the Military Affairs Commission, regarding temporary remedies for military training in high schools and above (3), free issuance of bullets for shooting exercises, please order the Ministry of Military Affairs to issue them free of charge by the Training Directorate General in the future, and the instruction within the approval is: 'It can be done as requested', and so on.' It should be handled accordingly. It should be notified and checked for filing and replied, etc. The above is approved. It is checked that this Ministry previously practiced live-fire shooting exercises in high schools and above, according to the method of borrowing guns and purchasing bullets. The schools are limited by facts, and it is still difficult to implement them universally. Therefore, it has been transferred to the public for ease of use to submit a memorial to Chiang Kai-shek, chairman of the Military Affairs Commission, requesting approval for free issuance to facilitate training, and the approval is: '(It can be done as requested)', etc., and the Ministry has also recorded it and consulted the Ministry of Military Affairs for filing and reply. Now it is approved that, in addition to forwarding the order, the bullets needed for live-fire shooting exercises by the schools in the future will be issued free of charge. The schools shall, in accordance with the plan, prepare and submit the exercise shooting roster on a regular basis to the National Military Training Committee for verification and submission to this Ministry for unified examination and handling. This roster must also be jointly signed by the principal and the instructors sent by the Ministry to be cautious. It should be notified accordingly, and it is hoped that it will be checked and followed, and transferred to high schools and above for compliance, etc." The above is approved. It is hereby urgently ordered to be notified.

Honors of Li Weining, Chinese Prodigy Musician 200

Praised by European Musicians

Li Weining, in his early twenties, is from Sichuan, China. He studied at Tsinghua University, but due to his love for music, he focused on this subject, leading to weaker performance in other subjects and preventing him from graduating. Later, someone recognized his musical talent and sponsored him to study in France, where he studied music for two years under the guidance of famous teachers, enabling him to make significant progress. He then entered the Vienna State Academy of Music in Austria, from which he has now graduated. He has achieved profound skill in music and is admired by musicians in various European countries. In mid-July of this year, during a large gathering, a certain famous Japanese musician composed lyrics, sang, and played the piano. Viennese people considered him just an ordinary pianist. However, when the young Chinese Li Weining composed and performed, everyone marveled at his talent as magical and rare. This was broadcast on the radio. The Vienna Daily News on July 17th reported: "The young Chinese composer Li Weining is a free student of Mr. Dan Di, the Dean of the Paris Conservatory of Music, and also a disciple of the Viennese musicians Max and Wieger. He broadcast his works on the radio, presenting them to the public. The music he played is part of his works, including a long piano variation and several songs. These works demonstrate his competence and mastery of European music. Professor Yang Boer performed this long piano piece and added 'Light and Splendid' (曲名). The listeners could not imagine that the composer of this piece was Chinese. This piece is very suitable for the piano, showing the author's deep understanding of the instrument's characteristics. The French listeners felt that Mr. Li's works were delicate and elegant, reminiscent of the French musicians Couperin and Dan Di, but with a romantic touch. The French considered it similar to the piano music of Schubert, Mendelssohn, and Schumann. The songs are full of Chinese flavor and rich emotion. The singer, Mr. Ruo Jita, has endless variations in his melody, which is very free and unrestrained, sometimes like a groan, and often has elements of grand opera. The sounds imitate each other at times. The strangest thing is that sometimes it sounds like European folk music, especially 'Thoughts on the Pond' (池上寓興) (a phrase from Bai Juyi's poem)." Also, the Times reported on July 18th: "Li Weining's Central European music adds luster to the Paris and Vienna schools, especially his variations and fugues, which express his Chinese heritage without any flaws and in the best possible way. On the one hand, he deeply understands and penetrates Western musical culture, and on the other hand, he has not damaged or forgotten his inherent Chinese nature. If he continues to work like this, he can introduce world music to China and simultaneously add ancient Chinese culture and characteristics to European music. Mr. Ruo Jita sang with a very detailed understanding, carefully translating the Chinese lyrics into German. The composer himself accompanied the songs on the piano, and his piano playing showed that he is a perfect Viennese pianist." Furthermore, the Austrian government newspaper also published praise, calling Li Weining from Sichuan, China, a genius artist who became famous in one fell swoop (words omitted for brevity). It is heard that a Chinese musician is called a genius and admired by famous European musicians, which is unprecedented. However, Mr. Li studies music at his own expense, and his situation is difficult. He has recently submitted a document to the Ministry of Education, recounting his painstaking efforts in studying music and his current difficulties, requesting a subsidy to continue his studies and bring glory to the motherland. It is hoped that China will cultivate outstanding musical talents and help him achieve his ambition to further his studies.

Announcement of Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association Scholarship 201

The Siming University Scholarship Committee, for the purpose of cultivating the studies of fellow villagers' children, who continue or enter domestic universities or research institutes with excellent academic performance, will, after application and approval, issue scholarships to encourage them. The details have been repeatedly recorded in this newspaper. It is heard that since the association set a registration deadline, the number of Ningbo students who applied for registration included: (1) eighty-four who continued their studies at university; (2) one who continued their studies at a research institute; (3) eighty-eight who entered university; (4) seven who planned to enter a research institute, totaling one hundred and eighty-eight. The review team members reviewed the applications according to the regulations. According to the review results, seventy-six names met the original standards, and twenty-four names met the qualifications but failed due to other allocation standards. It is heard that the association convened a full committee meeting yesterday. The attending committee members were Yu Qiaqing, Sun Hengfu, Zhang Shouyong, Liu Hongsheng, Wang Boyuan, Qin Runqing, Li Quanshi, Li Gufan, Hu Xi'an, Zhang Shenzhi, Wei Bozhen, Wu Yaqin, Hu Mengjia, Zheng Chengqing, Li Shuxiong, Yu Zuoting, etc., chaired by Director Wei Bozhen. The chairman reported on the review process, and it was determined that only seventy-six names met the original allocation standards after review. Among them, Zhu Peinong voluntarily waived his scholarship and should be given an honorary certificate. There were also twenty-four names that passed the review but were restricted by the allocation standards. The matter was submitted for discussion, and the following resolutions were made: (1) Those who passed the review and met the original allocation standards, except for Zhu Peinong, who voluntarily waived according to Article 10 of these regulations and will be given an honorary certificate by the association, the remaining students should, after the announcement, immediately go to the association with their guarantors to fill out the application form and guarantee. After completing the procedures, the association will directly submit the scholarship to the school where the student is studying for transfer. Those who are far away and cannot personally go to the association may have their guarantors send the application form, which the student should fill out and submit to the association. (2) It is noted that the first scholarship, originally set at one hundred and twenty-five slots, had different allocation standards for those who were already studying at university and those who were entering university, with further divisions into science, engineering, commerce, agriculture, medicine, liberal arts, and law. Students who had passed the review but failed to be selected due to the original allocation standards had excellent grades, and the current scholarship also had a surplus. A flexible approach should be adopted, borrowing slots from Category A to supplement Category B, and borrowing slots from Subject B to supplement Subject A, so that all students who have passed the review will not feel disappointed. The procedures for claiming the scholarship should also be handled according to the above items. (3) The association still has a surplus of scholarships. Any Ningbo student studying at a university who has excellent grades and applies for a scholarship according to the scholarship regulations will be allowed to extend the deadline to September 30th. This grand event of the Ningbo people has attracted the attention of the community. Followers are emerging, and some fellow villagers' associations are preparing to proceed. Next year, scholarship programs from various regions will spring up like bamboo shoots after rain, competing to initiate, which is a good phenomenon in the country.

Page 18

Free Talk

Third Anniversary (Part 1) 216

— Li Huiying

An autumn night.

From the open window, the night breeze carried wafts of the scent of grains. An indescribable joy welled up in Old Mrs. Huang's heart. She thanked the heavens for another good harvest this year. But then she immediately remembered an old matter, murmuring: (Just don't let it be like last year.)

Last year's harvest was excellent, but the grain couldn't fetch a good price. It was all the Japanese devils' doing, forcing down grain prices. Nine out of ten farming families in the village lost their capital. As for Old Mrs. Huang, although she didn't rely on farming to make a living, she always got a share of grain from the tenant farmers every year. In a year of good harvest, she could get a few more stones of grain. If grain prices were higher, wouldn't she be able to save a little money?

Old Mrs. Huang wasn't a miserly money-grubber, but circumstances forced her to have these small hopes.

(Ahem!...)

After a cough, she sighed again at her bitter, gentian-like fate. She had a good, proper family. Herself, plus two sons. The eldest son had taken a wife and even had a granddaughter. She was just waiting for her second son to get married, and then she would have completed her duty as a mother, and could enjoy a little happiness in her old age. But her fate was unkind (Old Mrs. Huang firmly believed in fate). Her eldest son was serving as a minor officer in the Changchun army, just about to make progress and bring honor to the family, when the Japanese soldiers suddenly became violent and occupied Changchun. Her son lost his life in that battle. He was a piece of flesh from her own body; how could she not be heartbroken? Later, when she heard the news, she cried as if she were dying. Fortunately, she still had one son left, which gave her a little comfort amidst her grief. She advised her daughter-in-law to put all her hopes on her younger brother-in-law, so that when he became famous, she, as his sister-in-law, would surely enjoy happiness in her later years. However, things were getting worse and worse. After the death of his brother, her second son ran away. He left secretly, leaving Old Mrs. Huang a simple letter, saying that he was joining the Volunteer Army to kill Japanese soldiers, to avenge his brother and others, to wipe out shame, and to recover lost territory. So, Old Mrs. Huang felt as if she had fallen from heaven to hell. She had no hope left, only a deep pain that could never be washed away.

She always thought of others, especially her daughter-in-law. She felt so sorry for her, widowed at such a young age, and without any hope for the future. How sad! One time, she spoke frankly to her daughter-in-law:

(You don't need to worry. Now that things have come to this, worrying is useless. I think it's like this: you can do whatever you want.)

But her daughter-in-law didn't listen to her. She continued to live her life, raising her daughter.

(Tomorrow is that day again?)

Old Mrs. Huang abandoned the scent of grain in her nostrils and let go of her painful memories. She reached for an almanac and looked at it under the lamp. Yes, tomorrow was indeed that day. She almost forgot. She folded a page in the almanac, marking it. There, printed in black ink on white paper, it clearly read:

(September 18th.)

She closed the almanac and called out to the outer room:

(Xiao Lan, come here.)

A five- or six-year-old girl came running in, bouncing and jumping, asking:

(Grandma, what is it?)

(Where's your mother?)

(My mother?)

(Yes.)

(She, she's lying down.)

Old Mrs. Huang understood and said urgently:

(Go, call your mother. Tell her I need her.)

The child left. Tears welled up in Old Mrs. Huang's eyes. Tomorrow, September 18th, would be the third anniversary of the day her eldest son died in the Changchun military camp. Three years had passed so quickly. She wiped her eyes and looked out the window. Outside, there was heavy darkness. Old Mrs. Huang dared not look. She quickly closed her eyes tightly. She imagined that the darkness outside was like the darkness and hopelessness that would engulf her family in the days to come.

The Northeast Volunteer Army 217

— Xicun

As the third anniversary of the September 18th Incident approaches, I would like to take this opportunity to discuss the issue of the "Red Armbands." I hope the readers will not consider this meaningless.

(What are the Red Armbands?) That's what you must be asking. Yes, I must first explain this term.

"Red Armbands" - no need to cite classics or give lengthy explanations. In a word, they are the Volunteer Army fighting the Japanese in the Northeast! Because they wear a red armband on their sleeves (that is, on their arms) as a mark.

It is said that last year was a bad year for the Red Armbands, but this year there has been a major turnaround. This has a history. A friend of mine who is a Red Armband recently came from the Northeast and told me about the situation.

Speaking of the bad luck of the Red Armbands last year, it was mainly due to the harm inflicted by the Japanese. The Japanese declared to the common people that the Red Armbands were bandits (they have always used this deception to fool the people), that they were disturbing the people, and were the people's enemy. Therefore, the people should try to defend themselves and fight the Red Armbands to the death. If they could capture one, they would be rewarded with money according to the rules. The average people have a very weak sense of national identity and have always preferred to live a comfortable private life. As a result, in order to covet money and maintain their comfortable state, they naturally needed to make things difficult for the Red Armbands and oppose them. Therefore, wherever the Red Armbands went, the people would use their own weapons to attack them head-on. Forced with no alternative and unable to gain a foothold anywhere, these struggling Red Armbands had no choice but to retreat into the mountains and subsist on wild grass and fruit.

At that time, no Red Armband dared to appear on rural roads alone, otherwise they would be in danger of losing their lives at any time.

In that period, the Japanese soldiers did not need to come out themselves, and they were able to subdue the activities of the Volunteer Army in the countryside.

The common people and the Red Armbands became enemies.

But this year, the situation is very different. Because the Japanese have collected civilian firearms everywhere since the spring, and have also forcibly seized land deeds, the people's livelihood is no different from being pushed to a dead end. As a result, with no way to go and no door to enter, they immediately took the risk. The people who used to oppose the Red Armbands have now become Red Armbands themselves, and the two sides have become brothers in distress.

Since the Red Armbands are having good luck this year, their actions are also much more convenient. Even if the people have not joined the organization, at least their impression of the Red Armbands has changed. They not only communicate with the Red Armbands, but also are happy to provide the Red Armbands with some supplies within the scope of their possibilities.

This also has a clear source. Since the Japanese soldiers confiscated all the civilian firearms in the Northeast this spring, whenever Red Armbands or even real bandits arrived in the summer, the people were helpless and unable to resist. This is one of the people's plights. In addition, when rural areas report alarms, Japanese soldiers never come to the countryside to protect them. It is not until after the Red Armbands have retreated that the Japanese soldiers arrive, but this is not helpful. They either arrest a few people and falsely accuse them of colluding with bandits, or they burn down all the houses in the area. This kind of abuse and persecution provides the Red Armbands with an opportunity to expand their power.

Now, Red Armbands can walk alone without weapons, and as long as they don't encounter Japanese soldiers, they will no longer encounter people's ambushes wherever they go.

This is an ironclad fact!

The development of the Red Armbands can only be reliable and promising if they are united with the people. This is why the Japanese soldiers dare not go to the countryside to search and suppress them.

Here is a rather comical thing: the security teams and police teams in the cities and towns of the Northeast now have yellow armbands as their mark, belonging to the (Manchu) country. People call them "Yellow Armbands." Recently, the yellow armband has been replaced with a red background on the back. This provides a convenience: if they encounter the Red Armbands coming over, they can turn the Yellow Armband mark over to avoid the Red Armbands' difficulties.

Some people may think that the development of the Northeast Volunteer Army has reached a standstill, and some even deny the existence of the Volunteer Army. I cannot agree with this. The number of Volunteer Army members is irrelevant, and the pace of development is also irrelevant. The most important thing is their firm confidence - their will - that is, their principles! The anti-Japanese armies of the past, some were bought off and some were sold out. They are all in the past and no longer worth mentioning. As for the current Red Armbands, they can be said to be true anti-Japanese warriors. Only they want neither money nor fame! They are more able to endure hardship, and their only mission is:

(To resist the armed aggression of Japanese imperialism to the death!)

We can say, wishing the Red Armbands victory:

(The Red Armbands are the true anti-Japanese peasant Volunteer Army.)
